O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the summary of medicine's knowledge at its end, and finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I saw in my vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of manual skills, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is practiced in our region and is everywhere unknown, so it has been lost and its knowledge has been taken away, and nothing remains from it beyond the small descriptions in books by the ancients that were handled by the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and closed minds, and science has been moved away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems I should revitalize this treatise altogether according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will follow together the forms of the cautery instruments and other tools for use with their adjustment and preparation, just as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters are found in our time for this reason, the art of medicine has been extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who interferes to master in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until they know the location of the limbs and their shapes and connections and separations, and have knowledge about bones, nerves and arteries, and the number of bones, and their movement and rest positions, and where their exit lies.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus says Hippocrates that rest with rest is much, and work with work is little; and similarly in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone is not aware of what has been said before, they might commit errors and waste others' time; just as I have seen many times more than once with those who interfere in this science and abandon their knowledge and lack of experimentation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who amputated one of the neck ulcers or a woman's goiter, and cut into her arteries around the neck; because so much blood came out that the woman died in her surgeon's hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in an elderly man, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to remove it, and saw the position of the wound and the size of the stone, and indeed if they operated on him he died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw one other case which was treated by draining Duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breakage there was an injury; and the patients were full of ignorance causing the break to occur in the wound from being treated roughly, and did not allow any healing at all for the injury, and did this until one month; and he was commanded not to move it again; so he stayed like that until his leg was completely swollen and his feet, and resulted in ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to relieve the leg; and when I heard it being dislocated so smoothly that he did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the corruption was already established or throughout a member, and could not be cured; and the corruption did not cease to spread within the member until the member was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see a second wound that collapsed an abscess in a crooked way, and then inflamed due to the mischief of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a gangrene, when it is of dark bile humor, one should not touch it with iron if it is in its place so that all the corrupted parts can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear children, you need to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: that is to say, one where there is danger in multiple dispositions; and I will show you in each section of this book where it has power and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary for you to keep this advice, so that the foolish might not wrongly speak of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your weapons in consideration, and treat your illnesses lightly but firmly, and use the best way so that through God's grace you come to salvation and be blessed; and leave the terrifying diseases without complaint of healing; and remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to another one with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galien states in some of his admonishments: "Do not take ill disease into treatment, lest you be called a foolish observer."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters deal with fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and the chapters are organized from the head down to stones; and about the shapes of instruments, and the metals for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the operation.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters concern cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar matters; and these chapters are organized with descriptions of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters deal with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters; and they are arranged from the head down to stones, and include descriptions of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we remember from the work, it is necessary for me to discuss the quality of each remedy and its harm associated with each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I state that the qualities of assistance, and the harm, are the longest word and subtlest science and the secrets respond. And many wise people spoke about this, agreeing with it; and they satisfy me with their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I state that the cautery helps universally for any complexion where there is matter, because there are two kinds of complexions: this means hot complexion with substance and dry complexion with substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry complexion combined with matter, they divided their thoughts and said that the cautery is a great aid. And the other group said the opposite: that the cautery only helps in diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot and should not be treated with hot illnesses by heat or drying. And it contradicts those who say otherwise, that the cautery provides great assistance to hot and dry diseases that come into the bodies of people.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the nature of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion by experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And for all procedures, do not interfere except that which has been proven and by long use is known the chapter of cautery, and the variety of human complexion, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and time period; we have no fear from other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the parts should assemble and align with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know this, my children, that assembling a fire-based cautery contains secrets of healing and yields even greater goodness than a burning medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth from any member that is cooked, and does not harm another member if it's not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	The fiery medicines spread from one part of the body to another, causing diseases in various parts; and sometimes they displease the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, due to its high quality and the goodness of its substance, does not cause this if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experimentation and the length of my service and study in the art, it aligns with the truth of things; and because of this, I apologize for the length of speech, as I do not wish to withhold from you the secret of fire and its quality, how it removes diseases from bodies, as the philosopher explains when demonstrating. Receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, boy, that they decided when the cauterizations should be done, and read prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, because the harms arising are most removed by the help of the cautery; and likewise if the cauterizations are for necessary pains that cannot wait until greater evil befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like those foolish people, child; for there is no recurrence to a disease cured by cauterization. They say it this way: but they are mistaken, because cauterizations are only medicine that changes the complexion and dries out the fluids causing pain, which is more effective than medicine for hastening recovery, and due to the power and authority of its work.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the possibility is that the disease does not return at all according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness and its effects; they are gathered together in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things. If no cauterizations are administered or if there's little excess and moisture, as with cauterizations for pain, and similar conditions, then this kind of pain does not return again; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And not many people understand why cauterizations are named the last of medicine, and this can be seen; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine. But their understanding is false, and they say cauterization is the last of medicine because when our methods for cures in any disease do not work, then we administer our cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Thus clearly cauterizations are the last of medicine, not according to the understanding of those who say otherwise.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauterizations are more effective than iron ones and they stated this because of the quality of gold and its high substance. They also mentioned that the skin under iron cauterizations does not rot; however, it's not true as I've proven it myself and found that in some individuals, it can indeed happen. Gold cauterizations are better than iron ones, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat the gold tool, you do not realize that it is heated by the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down; and if you heat it too much; then put it in fire; thus, there is enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our metal cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So I have organized this chapter about the shoulder joint up to the elbow, so that one may find it more easily.
dou cautere olivaire	oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The fire cautery works with moisture and cold on the brain. There are two ways to do it due to an illness called 'soda', and due to many fluids that descend from the head as sweat, from ears, and because of multiple dreams and toothache, throat pain, and especially for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is cleansed by a dissolving medicine altering the head. Three or four times, or five times according to how well the powers and the strength and the habit of the patient can bear it; and then wash off the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place his hands between yours and put your hands under his nose. After that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two nostrils; and let it come where your middle fingers are, if blood is drawn out, then heat up the cautery which is called 'olivare', from which here is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the joint in its natural position with ink, and guide your hand downwards and sideways gradually and steadily while turning it; then lift your hand alone, and check if you see bone. If you don't see any bone, continue with the cautery until you do see bone as I have instructed; after that take one pinch of sand, put a moistened cotton inside and place it in the joint, allowing it to be there for three days; afterwards apply a butter on top of a cloth; leave it on until the scorching disappears; then treat the wound with the ointment known as 'tetrafarmaçon', continuing until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they said that the older ones believed, when a wound stays open longer, more pus discharges out; and because of this advice moves.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And it was said by none of them that we should let the cautery burn for so long that part of the bone becomes ashes, and then one must set back what has been burnt from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say the other that we must let the cautery burn there and press so hard that it raises as wide like a small egg that women place in their bellies because fluids can be expelled out of it; and should we leave the wound open for a long time afterwards; after this, we should clean it and dress it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of using a cautery do not seem to me to be good in every respect, except when it comes to certain patients with fear; and I believe that I should leave them alone; because the joints become weakened by continuous exposure to nature's fluids, as we demonstrate with other limbs; and even when the joints are weak from nature itself, and my first experience of using a cautery is more healing and soothing for me, and in doing so I gather together salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the old head pain
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the entire head comes chronic pain that lasts for a long time, one should use the patient's fingers and pills which are called "cochies," and also do cleansing of the head and ears with bandages; and if one performs the cautery as we have previously mentioned to them, then it proves effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the shoulder of the patient is of strong nature and not too cold; therefore, apply the cautery slightly over the part where we previously mentioned to do so.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After apply the cautery to each horn of the head up to the bone, just as we have said previously, and perform one application of it over where it is called "vessel"; and make one application of it in the place where suction cups are placed; and lighten your hand so that you do not go beyond the bone: patients feel more intense pain with this cautery than others, and I will discuss this further elsewhere; and it should be noted that the applications to the horns should be subtler than that used for the middle part of the head, and it's the form:
dou cautere dou chief	A fire cautery, for the purpose of a patient, instructs them to let their hair grow long and even; and if it starts pricking at its base when they are young, one should hold steady so as not to move until they fully grow.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When pain suddenly comes to a part of the head and extends till to the eye, and if the shoulder is purged by mild medicines, and other treatments I mentioned about diseases have been done in the division of diseases, but none of them help: then one should do cautery according to two ways, meaning with medicine water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine water cauteries involve you taking a spoonful of oil, and then applying the bark and dressing to two pieces each for both shoulders, in such a way that you can place the spoonful of oil on the skin; and when it is placed, ensure it adheres well and leaves it like this for 12 hours. Then remove and treat with garlic butter until pus comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the oil cure until it is healed; and if you see that doing some of those burning medicines that I have written or the first treatment of burning medicines works for you.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is done in this manner. Heat up the shape of the cautery as described:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a bell or has .i. inch of curvature, and at the middle there's a small appearance; put it over the painful area, hold your hand and slightly rotate the iron, until half of the thickness of the flesh burns; lift your hand to avoid burning the artery, which will start bleeding abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After this, place cotton in the form of a bandage and keep it on the affected area for .iij. days; then apply moistened cotton with butter, and continue oil treatment until it heals completely; if you wish to cauterize this migraine using the iron cautery ('cultellare'), do so at its tip but be careful not to cover the artery in this part of the migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	From headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure headache as we have previously described in divisions of diseases, and it is not effective, and you notice that the cauteries mentioned earlier from medicine do not work on the iron, then it becomes necessary to heat the cautery known as "cultellare" until it turns white; and do this at a length of half a foot along the arm, and take your hand once, and strain until you no longer touch the artery and only reach up to the bone; and guard against the jaw that closes when eating, and let the tongue only care about closing and not allow spasms to affect the patient, and guard against bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if cutting it causes great fear and similarly for those who are untrained and inexperienced; and leave your work half done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery has been cut, and I will show you where it happens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you notice that these cauteries do not work on the illness, and the patients are suffering, apply them to the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you see this, use the cautery that we said or from chapter on extraction of the artery, with a two-bladed cautery; and these cauteries are better than that one and more effective.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from cold in the ear, and we have tried remedies that dissolve and others of the treatments we discussed in this division, and if the pains do not subside, then apply this type of cautery called 'points', which is described thus:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez. de la torture de la bouche	of mouth agony
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Tortures that should be cured by cautery are only those that move due to the flow of blood, as we have stated in the divisions of diseases; and no cautery is to be done for those that come from scorching and inflammation of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this kind of torture that moves due to the flow of water and from clearing the head, as well as gargling, if it responds well, then it is necessary for you to apply the cautery with three applications: one in the root of the ear, and another slightly beyond the temple area, and the third at the adjustment between the two lips; and place the cautery on the healthy part that opens up, and apply it right where the head of the ear is just under a bit above the ear wax, and another on the temple as long as about an inch; and leave the cautery there until half the skull is burned; and this is how you should do the application of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there is the appearance of the cutler's burn that we have described previously, but it is somewhat more subtle and requires that the knives be a bit thicker; after the treatment of the area as I have said before, until it becomes healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with an old stroke, you treat it as we have said, and if it does not benefit, and the patients do not have a fever, then let him undergo four cauterizations: two on each of the four head corners, one under the head, and one on the neck in what is called 'watches' as we have mentioned before, and the last one at the mouth of the stomach; and treat it accordingly as we said previously.
de litargie	from Liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, you should give the patient large pills and brain-purifying pills to cleanse their brain; afterwards, let them rest with their head high. And place the camphor plaster on the back of the head; and here is how you do it like a cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it remains in this state, well and good; and if not, let him undergo three cauterizations down the neck to just below the collarbone, and leave an interval of one finger's width between each cautery. And treat as with others, and if you see it fitting together, and the patient endures, let him undergo a third cauterization in the middle; and if required, two more on top of the two horns, and treat until it is in this state; and let the cauterizations be called 'olivare', as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	Of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed of years and what we have said before; after treating the head with the patient, then let him undergo cauterization down the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine below the neck; and if you need more, and if the body is moist and the patient endures, and the disease has spread, then let him receive four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave until the most pleasant cure becomes dry, and lift your hand; afterwards treat until it is in this state, and let the cauterizations be called 'olivare' as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	From epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine. Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	And if the organs are female, make one subtle cautery according to this manner:

When due to the reason of melancholy are excesses or substances corrupted and large bile flows, therefore the part cautery of fire cauteries as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division. After removing the head of the malady; afterwards make two pieces of linen well made, as one circle, put them under the head; and if the malady is seated, place it so that it is held in all directions; after that present the liniment, and apply butter from old beeswax; and heat it on a moderate fire, until what you pour can be tolerated; afterwards empty the circle through the center with the head under it, and let it cool; and do this to each part of the malady once per week with another good method, until it is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you see that the cauterization has been done by making several burns throughout the entire area of the cautery. This method of cautery moistens the brain more significantly; and then place damp cotton, butter, and gelatine fat on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the pain in the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the pain first comes to the eyes through the symptoms I have mentioned in the division, then start and continue to instruct the patient on things that purify the head, and keep him/her away from all moistures, and make him/her sweat or take baths several times fasting.

After having him/her direct his head, and make him/her cauterize in the head area, and make two cauterizations on each temple when the pain subsides from both eyes together, or when the pain is subsiding only from one eye; and apply this cauterization to all veins and arteries that are around the brain, and make sure they are cauterized long according to the width of the temples; and watch for bleeding out, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it properly like you did before.

And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incisions in the cautery technique how to perform it; and never should one apply a cautery or heat over both sides of the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the two paths of tears

And if further treatment is needed, carefully perform one small cautery up to the eyelid for each location.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the two paths of tears within the eyes

Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called 'claw':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the oil has been softened due to illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this type of cautery which is called 'olive'. And if you see that it's done twice, two cauterizations on the two nipples as long as they are; and don't let go of the hand until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the method I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No instance has occurred where the hair of the eyelashes turns into the underlip and pricks the eye; in that case, one performs cauterization according to two methods: namely, with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in good health; after that draw a figure on the paper of the eyes such as it is like to the leaf of mirtle, and let its beginning be at the sign of between the hairs; then place wet cotton saturated with egg white and garlic paste on the eye, then heat up the fire cautery which has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that cauterize on the figure you have drawn bit by bit several times, until the skin is blackened in that spot; and the signs of health are that you see the paper shrink, and the hairs lifted to the eye's point. Then raise your hand and leave thus for three days, then place wet cotton saturated with butter until the scorching disappears; after that apply a balm until it heals properly.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs and paper are softened, then restart with the cautery on that same area as you did before. If the hairs have fallen out, apply heat until the paper rises to its natural position and is even, without touching the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The fire cautery of medicine commands the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; then make a shape from parchment as if it were the leaf of myrtle. Then take French soap and live charcoal, each one ounce, and grind them together thoroughly; mix it quickly so that it doesn't cool down, then spread it over the shape like a myrtle leaf, put it on the paper eyes. If the disease is only in one oil, you must open it with one finger, if in both equally; place cotton moistened with egg white under each eye. The patient's shoulder be in your good health and put your forefinger showing on the medicine; press once every two times when the patient feels the bite of the medicine because they feel a bite also like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, then apply the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting sensation has passed, then raise your arm from the wound, and if you see that the paper is raised in the same way as it was lifted due to the constriction of fire or incision; and if this is so, then it is well. If not, then apply more medicine on your finger or where the medicine hasn't worked, until all your actions are equal and your eyes are in order; then place moistened cotton with butter under them until the burned flesh has healed, after that cleanse the arm from the ointment called 'dyafenis' and others, until it is healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if it is necessary that you guard well in your work by great caution so that no medicine sticks to the eye. And if the paper becomes moist after, and the hairs pinch in the eye, then repeat the medicine on the part of the eye which has softened from clean paper; do this as you did previously; after that treat until it is healed completely; and this is the form of the leaf of rue:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are various in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and do not allow the right way to that person who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have instructed in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you apply cautery to them according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in a healthy position; and cut the hair on his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shift his head; after this, apply moistened cotton inside an egg or garlic juice to the eye; then heat the cautery which is prepared: and place it close to the head as if it were a feather of a rooster, so that the tip of the cautery rests there; if you see it, let the tip point from one part of the head to another, and if you can see it, let it be like a tent; but in any case, it is better for your work that it not move.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, and treat any pus, then dry it off; and if it is closed, operate on it, remove from the bowe; afterwards place the heated cautery in this manner, hold your hand near the cautery to the part below the eye, so that your hand does not cause trouble; and put the cautery into the oil grease, and let it fume.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you start with the cautery until the bone, it would be good. If not, continue with the cautery one more time, and if needed, do so again, then leave it for three days; afterwards, place moist cotton on balm, and apply the dry ointment cure as long as it's healing. And if forty days pass without healing, put on a corrosive water medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow this method according to what you find in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a method for cauterizing fistulas that none of the old ones mentioned. Understand what a fistula is and perform it; afterwards, place one thin camel bone in the slit.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they do it in the size of three parts of a spoon; and hold your hand or camel firmly, making sure not to move the patient's skin so that the melted wax does not drip onto their eye; and one should put moistened cotton on the eye before applying an egg yolk or oil: the wax then removes the pus from the boil, and through marvelous healing, it saves health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, that is good. de l’aposteme de la goule	of the boil on the neck
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or on the gland, or at the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it turns rotten and swells up and becomes discolored, turning into a fistula; then you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not heal: so you need one cautery according to the size of the fistula; after removing the pus from the fistula, keep your hand until the iron tip reaches the bottom and beyond the lesion; do this process once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is healthy; if it heals like this, it's good; and if not, you need to uncover the area and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in your medical text.

de la dolor des dens	from toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu. Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Wax cautery if it's like this: you take butter from a cow, and at the tip of a metal or iron spoon; after that take cotton and wrap it on the point of a needle, and moisten the cotton with melted butter, then put it quickly over the painful tooth and hold until it cools down; and do this often until its effectiveness reaches to the root of the tooth. And if you see cold hair and cotton moistened in cooled butter, apply it again onto the painful tooth, and place a hot iron on it until heat from the fire reaches to the nerve of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery if it's like this: you take a piece of iron or steel, and make it large enough so that the flame doesn't reach to the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, from which its heat will come afterwards, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the heat from the cautery cools down; do this repeatedly, for the pain will be alleviated that day or the next. And ensure that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in anticipation of this cautery, then remove the fire; and this is how the cautery works:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery to the extent that you wish it, and according to what is within your ability; this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	of the tumors
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez. When you handle the metal tip, if it resembles a small rasp, and then heat the rasp completely until it's red hot; leave your hand touching until the cautery touches the place where the metal tip is cut; do this once or twice, and if there are many metal tips, cauterize each one just like we have said; after applying healing herbs wait until they start to heal; and if you heat a large cautery on iron, it will provide greater help.
de plaie mal curee	from poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening the wound, as we will explain in its proper place, if there arises a disease that can only be cured through the use of a cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is no opening present, and the condition worsens with gangrene and infected moisture, it's necessary to thoroughly examine and test every detail of this case. Always be aware of how much damage each area has incurred.
de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide. de la vessie	From the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is thick and weak from heat and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you should apply a cautery to the lower part of the bladder, where hair begins on the hand, and one each right side and left side; and let each cautery be as long as our finger. And make an application defuers (backwards) across the back, or two if needed; and let the cauteries form in a clavile shape according to what was said beforehand.
de la marris	From the maris
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	From the thigh
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous fluids descend into the thigh socket, and because of this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the leg is longer than the other when measured together; and it's found that the limbs start from their origin view, so you should cauterize the wound on the thigh socket as if with one cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the limb within the socket where it turns, so that the socket be inside the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those which have been cauterized on the stomach.

de la dolor de la hainche	Of thigh pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the buttocks region, and this is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient has been treated as we have described for division and treatment of such cases without success, and the disease is old: therefore, it is necessary that you cleanse the body of thick fluids using stinking pills or other good-looking pills.

Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars. Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. And this is the way it's done in sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and doesn't reach up to the thigh or down to the leg. And if it does come up to the thigh and the leg, then two cauterizations are performed at the place where the pain resides, and one above the ankle three inches, on the left side a little bit; and make these cuts with the surgical blade, and burn away any thickened areas of the skin. And if the person feels that the pain extends up to the knee or close to it, cauterize there where they feel the pain at three points or four points, where points are referred to in this process.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if more work is needed, then do it accordingly; and if the pain spreads from the knee towards the thigh, perform a cauterization with the surgical or circular blade. Make sure to take great care in all your cauterizations so that you don't let up on burning until you've destroyed nerves and major arteries, and don't cause the patient any greater harm or constriction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen several who performed cauterizations on the ankle up to the knee, and left them until the leg was swollen all over, and also the feet were so affected that they became inflamed and rotten. After this procedure of abdominal washings, death ensued for him.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, make cauteries on each one following this manner. // And the surgeon says concerning the fire cautery of the thigh, as follows, take one such iron rod that is as large as a small duck or slightly smaller, and have it intricately designed with lines running through it from the start to the other end, across both parts; let there be two crossing points, making them resemble knots, and prepare two sturdy iron rods. Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it turns completely red and emits steam, then place the heated rod on the afflicted part of the thigh, turning it towards the healthy side; apply one cautery operation at once to each side and leave the area for three days; then cover it with butter and keep the wound open as long as needed; continue treating with ointments until the wound heals.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use very little of this type of cautery for the fear of his consideration, and we see few who use it; yet still, this is a good cautery, which one can tolerate, and leaves where it has been applied.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by fall or from percussion or due to excessive evacuation, or due to any semblance of cold spread material, none of these appearances warrant cauterization, because it's akin to what comes from an infusion of cold matter.

Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often befalls small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they appear pale when they stand up and faint; and you find in the last spinal segment of the back and also on us the appearance that comes over the other spinal segments.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this [condition] and observe its treatment, if you apply it with a blood cautery in the form that follows.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. If you see this and observe the treatment, apply it using a proper blood cautery to each part of the spine equally. After that, let the area heal until it is sound according to what we have said, and be careful not to administer the cautery in places where there might be nerve congestion.

And should the pains descend to the knees and back, you administer the cautery as we have described in our chapter. For should you give him good care and purge phlegm, he will be restored by God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the uterus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture occurs in the stomach and the intestines fall into the cervices (birth canal), this is new. It is necessary that when you see it being cured, do not remove it during day; and use things that relieve the belly, so that the insides descend from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to rub his anus until the intestines are repaired, then take them with your fingers, and pinch just under the rupture onto the bone of the knee, and have it look as if there is a sign halfway up the front, like half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery to its form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Until it is white and emitting faeces. Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to stand up, he should be assisted by a well-made bandage and wear it for forty more days; with good rest, he should move lightly and avoid overeating or drinking excessively and shouting too loudly; and once he follows this advice, he is entirely restored.
