de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from old pain in no member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from falling or being struck, and that pain lasts long, and the cure of medicine does not help, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "points", and the cauterizations according to the length of the member, its smallness and weakness, its utility, and its location for twisting and its pain. If the healing is good from the first cauterization, that's fine; if not, perform another second cauterization on it, because such a routine is that it should change in relation to the body part that is closest to it, so you must make the cauterizations until the patient feels better.
de meselerie	In amalgamation
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The meseil are treated with a cautery once in a while and, likewise, the disease that originates from the putrefaction of blood and melancholy. If you see it being cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and treat it according to what we have said in division, without letting it spread or persist, and doubt that corruption might permeate all the meseil, then perform .v. cauterizations on the chief: .i. on the head up to the ninth degree, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and .ij. on the .ij. horns, and .i. behind on the hinge; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches down to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors from the large humors can escape; and cauterize it on the mice according to what was described previously.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the meseil is scattered everywhere; and it clearly manifests itself, so it's necessary that you cauterize using these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cauterization under each nose, and two cauteries along the spine from the neck, and seven along the spine of the back, and a large one over the kidneys and another in front, and two along the shoulders; and two across the ribs, and two along the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of hands and feet, and in the cavities of the hands; and be careful not to burn any nerves that are behind the heel bone, so do not scorch them. And never make a cauterization over the bone at the elbow, and another over the bone of the stomach, and one more on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when I use the fire cautery more often, I provide more aid, and it benefits; and know that patients do not feel pain during cautery as healthy people would, because their bodies are already thoroughly corrupted. And ensure that your cautery tools are both large and small according to limbs and joints, as you will find in manuals for instrument use. After the cure, dust the area with flour mixed with honey and other treatments until it is completely healed.
de enfleure	of inflation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling appears in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it doesn't heal, then I make cauterizations on the limb according to the size of the limb; and so let the cauterization go just a little into the skin near the bone. Then treat it with dressings until it heals. And every time one makes a cauterization at the wrist, at the foot, and at the back, along the exit point of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, in this way the swelling is extracted; and still, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	From balms
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease known as "albaras" progresses and medicine in the form of remedies proves ineffective, then apply heat from a cautery slightly over its surface, according to the thickness of the blood found there, until the pus is removed and the color changes; then clean with flour mixed with lentils and rose oil, plantain leaves, and blood from a sheepdog and an almond, each in their respective parts; mix all together, wrap it with a cloth, and leave on that part until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for the chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the chancre begins to appear, and you want to halt its progress, then apply a cautery around the circumference of .1 circle, all around the chancre. And still, some say that one should also apply the cautery in the middle of the chancre; and I personally do not think this is wise, as I fear it might lead to ulceration and putrefaction, which has happened on several occasions for me; and a more prudent action would be to cauterize around it, with a cautery known as "circular", just like we have described earlier in terms of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When some have a disease called "adubelati", and it is delayed from dying or because of its excess or due to the old age of the body when it is decrepit (that means too old) and it has little blood, or due to tension; and you see that it hastens towards death: then apply small cauteries inside by making a few minor ones; leave him like this. For it will hasten its death.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that it penetrates the entire cauterization, then heat the cautery as described here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterizations have penetrated through the kidneys, and make such cauterizations that the patient feels relief to such an extent that the process of decay is alleviated. After treating him until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment with fire using a metal tool
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of disease is called 'corrodens', and it's nothing else but a member disease, because it affects the limbs like the fire affects dry wood. If you see this disease in someone who can withstand cauterization together with heat, then smooth out the cauterizing iron rods both small and large as needed depending on where the disease is; after that, cauterize from all sides until you remove all corruption, and leave nothing behind, making sure every rotten part is removed. And then let it rest for three days, and apply ointment with oil to those areas cauterized until the burnt parts are healed and all the corruption is gone. After that, perform the treatment of ointments that produce flesh. And if after three days you see no signs of healing, it's good; but if this doesn't happen, reapply the cauterization on the remaining corrupted area. This disease can sometimes be treated with medicine instead of fire cautery in someone who can tolerate heat cautery; however, fire cautery is more effective, and I've already mentioned the treatment of fever in a separate section: use it when needed.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The text discusses conditions that come with stones.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes when nails grow out, a disease is born which we call "clos" according to our understanding, and it's a large clotting thing that hurts the foot. And for this illness of clos, there are two ways to handle it: fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery involves heating up one tool like a feather from a goose, made of good iron in proportion so as to be able to pierce any nail all around, with fine margins; after that you heat the whole thing on top of the nail, and quickly twist your hand around the nail until it reaches the very tip of the nail; then leave it like this for three days until pus starts to form. Then make a plaster of dried soap powder mixed with vinegar, and let the plaster stay overnight on the entire area, and the nail will come out and be completely removed from its root. Then apply ointment healing balm until the wound is clean.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they're turning outwards in the flesh, and it happens many times whether in the hands or in the feet, then you must bring back hot water cautery; and do this way: take a thread of spider or iron, or a goose feather, and place them over the nail and its root. This is for things like warts; put the thread so that it touches everything around. Then add a bit of hot water, and hold your hand well while twisting it back until the edge of the thread reaches to the base of the nail, and then can find the way of the hot water deep down to the root; let the patient suffer for a little time with the hot water for an hour; then leave them like this, and they will completely come out from all their roots. Do this again as many times as you have nails in your flesh, until these are all removed from you, then heal any pus-producing wounds that may form.
li cure dou trembler	He heals by shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shudder from cold or nerves, or from a quartan fever or another sickness, it is necessary that you apply four or five cauterizations on the spine of their back. One cauterization between each spinal bone; and one cauterization at the chest, under the olive-shaped cauterization; if they continue to shudder, hasten their recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	pus-filled boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever you see the spot that has emerged or pus-filled boils coming from large putrid matter, if they originate from gross materials. It is necessary at first when they appear that you cauterize on each tip of every boil: a delicate firewood cautery stick, whereby its point grasps the flame, or a long root of aristolochia, or with an olive-shaped cautery iron. And it must not be cauterized immediately when they are just emerging, according to this manner, for they can't grow further into infection but instead, the excess that causes them is removed and they become healthy; yet it should be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound come outwards or during incisions on an abscess, and similar things; it is much distressing to smell it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless, whenever this happens to no one, if you hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein and hold it as tightly as possible until his pulse is calmed under your finger, and that no more drops come out; then light several small and large olive oil cauteries until they are all red. Then take one or many according to the size of the wound and apply them where the artery was running, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until his pulse is fully restored.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, then quickly take another one of the cauterizing instruments that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to perform this one after the other until the tooth becomes black; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve which is beneath, and that no harm comes upon the patient; and know that when the tooth comes out of the artery, it cannot remain well even if the artery is large, unless this is done through one of these four methods that we have mentioned: by cautery, by extraction if it has not been treated already, by strong string tying, or by medicines placed upon it which have the power to harden blood; and let it be tied and restrained in due course.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer hardening through tightly binding with cloths or placing things that burn upon it, or similar actions, if they do not benefit in this way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no means or medicine at hand, so they should place their index on the wound of the artery in the manner that we have said, and stretch it well until the area above the wound and above the artery is hardened; and do not move the finger but dampen it with cold water often as much as can be cold until the tooth becomes frozen and swollen and hardened. And prepare for cautery and medicines for what needs them.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for surgery
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all about every disease for which it is necessary to apply a fire cautery, or medicine that heats up, and we discussed their uses, causes, instruments, and forms of application; and I put that chapter dealing with the head until the feet, and now I will proceed in this chapter along the same route as those things are found more easily for what you want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this one, it is necessary for you to know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first book about cautery, so here greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to embark in folly. For many ways of people come into cures. Some come from those who were so afflicted by their illness that they died lightly due to the panic they find in their disease, and out of the terror of their malice; and against these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And there are some among these who give their understanding and say: "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is deceitful. It would not be appropriate for you to consent to those who come to your aid in this manner, but place more restraint in your honor than in your greed, do not act foolishly but wisely of those whom you are certain about and can have knowledge from; and use prediction and guidance in treatments of diseases where health has been converted; and this will help you gain good reputation, glory, and lasting memory for a long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of their hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have instructed you this chapter by discussing chapter by chapter, according to what is before or the chapter on cauteries, which I discussed from head to heel, because you will find it easier for that which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full of water at its head
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this sickness comes very often to children at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the head of the child; and it happens none other time because of some reason that cannot be identified.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this sickness happen outside of children, and among all those that I have seen, their death came quickly; and because of this, it seems to me that I should abandon the practice of this disease with such remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child of these, his shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day so much that it could not bear anymore; and he thought it to be too much moisture until he died, and this moisture is assembled right over the bone under the siphon, between the heart and the bone; and the veins are like this when the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and abscesses are small that you cut through the head a wide crack; and it's as long as two fingers, as long as the moisture flows; and see here the shape of the spathile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more extensive, and the abscesses are larger, make two cuts in the manner of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the symptoms you see are that the corners of the head open on each side, and the water jumps when you press it from your hand inside, and this does not respond to treatment: then it is necessary that you make three cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all moisture outside. After that, hold the cuts of linen and powders; then apply wine and oil, and leave it like this for five days; afterwards, reset the limb, treat the wound with poultices and applications, and let the head rest equally, then allow the patient to eat dry meat from a source without moisture as long as the member is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look at where the large opening of the abscess is, and the assembly of the water; for it is not always in front; nor always behind; neither always on the right; nor always on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut accordingly where the abscess opens and the water filling it, making the incision according to what you can do, and watch that you do not cut the artery; let a flow of blood, so that the patient dies due to the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of cautery by fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it comes to any illness that is called "catarrh" affecting the eyes or at the bottom of them, and this sickness is ancient, and the medicine cure doesn't help, then the last resort treatment if is the cautery with which one cuts off the two main arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you cover the eyes, make sure they are under their head; after this, rub a rough cloth on the area until the arteries become visible. Then stretch the patient's neck over two cloths so that the neck can be seen clearly. Next, look where the vein lies and examine both eyes after them being positioned just behind the ears, and once they've settled down, then mark the eyes with an X, and cover each one with a sharp spatula blade for about half an inch until you reach the bone, and this should be done while the head is elevated.

Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a cloth and wring out cold water, then place it on the ear, and apply other treatments that stop bleeding, which include therapies involving distillation processes.
de la char des papieres	From the ashes of the papers

de la gresle	From the ice block

de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of granules

des poilz des papieres	"Des poils de papier" translates to "paper hairs". This phrase might be used metaphorically or in a technical context depending on the broader context of the text. Without additional context, this could refer to fine threads or fibers that resemble hairs from paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. It is necessary for you to place the head of the eye in its healthy position, then turn over the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it turns correctly, that's good; otherwise, if not, you should pierce one thread at each of the two ends. de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding the corruption of the eye

Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	When it comes to working on the nose and moisture reaches up to the palate, you should know that there is blood present. And if the moisture doesn't penetrate as it should, you should know that there's new tissue above the bone, so no tools come forth for cutting: thus, one must first push out .i. threads of linen, a bit thick, and tie them with your hands; have an inch or less space between each knot; place the patient's head by threading these strands through their nose to their mouth, pull gently until it comes out through the nose into the mouth; children often do this in school, and it is a simple task for anyone who wishes to perform it. Hold one coming out of the nose with your hand, and another coming from the mouth with the other hand, understand each after the other as we are holding them here. Do this until you can tell that the knots have rotten the flesh inside; then pull out the threads, drain any blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and place it back into their nose as before; do this for three or more days if necessary, until the ointments dissolve all remaining flesh. Then put a paste of opium into your nose for several days once it is healed; and if there's need for dried medicine use them, this is how to use the instrument to clean out the head: one distills oils and medicines with the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And use silver or lead, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and guide it in the same way; and if you see fit, make a closed cane, and fill these tools to clean out the head; and have one hand for holding the head when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh of the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times in the head there arises a disease called "telul", it grows and becomes large to look at; because of this you should cut it off at the beginning, and remove all bone, then put on the head the cautery or hot medicine; and if you delay cutting until it is large, when it is hard, notice if it has turned color, lost sensation: do not touch it with iron as there's an abscess inside; because once cut, great harm can come to the patient. And if the abscess is due to heat touch, not from changed color, and you see that it can be completely cut off, let the patient bleed freely under fear, and cure him of dry things and restraining substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions for continuation come into one of these open veins, it doesn't benefit much, as this happens in few people. Therefore, such situations should not occur to anyone else; if the wound is still fresh and all its blood is evident; then adjust the two lips according to a stitch pattern, and cure them until they heal properly; and if both lips have turned white on one side and the other, it is necessary that you burn every part of their keratin so long as they heal, then join the two lips with a stitch and keep them in place, and sprinkle dragon's blood powder and powdered incense on them. Then apply a piece of plaster of Paris or another adhesive plaster, and leave it until it heals by itself, and cure with ointment until healed properly.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the solution: or with needles, as we have said in the stomach stitch; or with thread, which I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	Of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the mouth, within the lips there are abscesses that are hard like grains, smaller and larger in size. Therefore, you should open the lips and cut into each lump individually, then remove them with forceps from every part; afterwards, apply the mouth to a vitriol incision until the pus is drained out completely; then empty it gently, and clean the mouth of dry things until it heals fully.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, a whitish substance is born on the gums, which the old called "albulus"; it must be held in tweezers and cut at its root. Allow blood or blood to flow out of the wound; then place on the site with vitriol powder, or other drying and constricting powders. If that flesh returns after cutting, and does so many times, if it is cut a second time, and cauterize: if it doesn't return after the cautering; these are the forms of substances used to cut.
des sordens	of the stinks
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Many times they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, where the skins are ugly and rough; and many times the tooth becomes black and yellow with wormholes until corruption reaches the gum, making the tooth stink; it is necessary to hold the patient in your hands and his head so that you can see the teeth or the skin appear, until nothing remains. And thus make it smelly and green, yellowish and other colors, until they are removed; if what is extracted at the first attempt is suitable, it's good; otherwise, start again from the second day to the third, until you have everything out. Know that each tooth requires different cutting instruments for extraction according to its work shown by the dentist, as the remover of teeth outside the teeth has other forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you ready.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat someone for toothache pain, delay the extraction as long as possible because doing so is not bad; indeed, it's a very high substance up to this point where there should be no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is compelled to extract, ensure that you are certain about which tooth hurts. Often with tooth pain, be careful if it's a healthy tooth, and remove the good tooth; however, do not completely relieve the pain until the bad tooth is fully removed, as we have already determined this for these patients; and when you are certain about which tooth hurts, ensure to cauterize around the tooth thoroughly throughout i. spatumile firmly so that the gum stays in place from all sides; then move it between your thumbs or with your delicate forceps at a gentle tap-tap, until it is properly extracted, then secure well the forceps; and have the head of the patient below their knee, and hold firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if there is no sudden release of pain, take none of these instruments and gently push into each part inside the mouth, and then move them as you did initially. And if the teeth are pierced or damaged, ensure to fill them with cloths at the place where they lost. And when extracting subtly with forceps, make sure it does not break during extraction; and one must very carefully work around the gum for ease of removal of the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And make sure to guard that you do not break it, and leave a part undone, causing the patient more intense pain from the root of the mischief than before. And be wary not to act like ignorant surgeons who in their haste and boldness break everything once, not bringing any improvement as we have described; but instead they bring this great disease back through the opening of these roots that remain, or through breaking the cartilage, which happens often, just as we frequently say. And when the bone has been pulled, wash the area with wine or oil and vinegar; and if bleeding occurs, which often does, wash the area with vitriol solution; and if this doesn't work, apply a cautery treatment.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The tools you use to pull out the teeth, which come into contact with the tooth first, should have long points and thick handles, so they do not bend when you are pulling a tooth; these are the types of tools:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have thick limbs that do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-crafted iron, and should have teeth for gripping during use.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root stays in the extraction, it is necessary to place cotton moistened with butter inside. For one or two days, until the gums are softened, then use the forceps called "algefri", which makes the tooth appear as if cared for; and do this also like a file, this is its form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these forceps, it is necessary that you expose the entire flesh around the root, and put in the tool called "althali", which is known as pincers, this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it strong and large enough so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, use all tools, as their forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool which has two prongs, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other tools that are positioned before in the row of teeth, and with this tool that looks like a large pair of forceps, here is its form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And may these tools be such that they cannot be broken, and know that many instruments for teeth exist; and similarly with other tools which are not numbered; and let the wise master find his own instrument by himself, according to what his tasks and illnesses demonstrate to him. For there are parts of diseases where the old ones did not teach any tool because of the diversity among these, and if they break nothing from the caries or of other bones, or if it rots, then he seeks for the tools that suit him, which I have told you about, and aids in gestures, here is its form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well holding for keeping the bone, so it does not escape, but can keep and remove it; and then restore the site with medicines suitable to this, and if there is rot in the bone, and if it is small, then take all of this instrument to retrieve it.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and its shape is ugly, especially in maiden women, you should know if this tooth has been born after the real tooth, and it's not straight; then you can't file or grind it. Therefore remove it; and if it is mixed with the real tooth, take this instrument that is described here which has a form like half of a small beak, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file grinds slowly in your hands due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you don't move the others; and if it is visible that one can grind it, then use a single piece file as described here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And similarly to how one makes needles with the steel from nails; and by grinding down a tooth gently in short bursts, so that it does not move until it is thin; then in the end grind away completely without leaving any burr. And if the edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must smooth down the roughness of the edge until it is even, so as not to hurt the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth becomes dull
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front becomes loose, either by shaking or by hitting, and the patient is unable to push it out with what they chew because it doesn't fall out; if you have treated the area with medicines that restrict movement, and this didn't work. Then you should restrain it with a thread of gold; for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is dislocated, if it's returned to its place, again and again, as we've said; and do not interfere with someone who isn't a professional or suffers from pain, and each time shape it like an osine (a type of bone) tooth, and put it in the position where the defect is, and hold it like we've said, and remains and serves thus for as long as needed.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of covering the wound on the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	None of the veins that come from under the tongue or naturally present at birth; or by accident due to injury that is healed; and these operations are such that you work on the mouth with the aid of medicine, having your head in a healthy position, lift the tongue; then cover the nervous vein so large, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or stiffness, especially from sudden injury, if I cut the uncinate and cover it with something large; and be careful that the cut isn't too deep, for fear of an artery being underneath; and when you have done this, raise the head to pinkish water and cool water, then put under the tongue a linen cloth; and treat your illness every night so that the mouth cannot heal. And if bleeding continues, place vinegar in the mouth; and if it doesn't stop, cauterize with slow fire, which is good for such cases; then cure with other treatments until it heals completely.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it being of any color or black or hard, such that the patient doesn't feel it, and doesn't touch it either, because it's a chancre; and if it has started to turn to blenchor, and there is moisture, if pus secretes, and one cuts with a fine needle, and discharges from both sides; and if it refuses you in your operation, then apply vitriol oil until it is completely cleaned out. Then return to your operation as long as you're removing all the force. Then raise the limb from the side and the heel, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	None of the times does anything come within the throat that are called 'godath', and properly they are known as two almonds. And when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and if they're not healed, be cautious: if it's a small, hard abscess with any color inside, don't touch it even with iron. And if it is red and its root is large, don't touch it even with iron, also because of the bleeding; but let it until it bleeds on its own, and then you will remove it, or it would break by itself. And if it's a white colored abscess and its root is thin, prepare your instrument to cope, but first look to see if the abscess has healed and calmed down. Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and their head be in your line of sight when they are well, and let them open their mouth with servants holding their hands, and squeeze their tongue completely over the instrument, as shown here; and may it be silver or finely arain like knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue to all this instrument and see the abscess, if one takes an ounce and puts it into the almond, and moves it above as much as you can; and removes nothing from the threads with it. Then control the tool, from which this is shaped, like some strength; and always make the head bent, and each to its place, and are very sharp, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument now, take the tool from which this is shaped:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be it sharp on both sides and named; and when you have done one almond cut, do the other in the same manner, and after incision gargle the patient with hot water, or water that is hot and easy to drink, and if bleeding occurs, gargle with hot water, or with cooked currant almonds, or bay leaf, or similar things, until the wound has healed; then treat them until they are well; and let no new abscesses form in the throat other than the two almonds, so cut them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, to be precise, a small-sized abscess. She almost completely had the entire throat closed off due to it, so she couldn't breathe through the obstructed passage and consequently couldn't eat or drink, thus dying if she remained like this for one day or two. The abscess had risen to such a point that four inches of rope were needed for each of the two openings at her neck. I immediately proceeded with urgency, placing an inch of rope in one opening, then pulling it out and extracting a large portion of the pus; afterward, I placed another piece of cloth around this other opening, and forced her mouth open while pressing on her tongue; after that, I placed the inch of rope inside these abscesses, taking out some pus with it. Only a little blood came out from here; thus, the throat passage was unobstructed for the woman, she started now drinking water and then wine, and didn't stop cutting away at this abscess over a long period of time; and the abscess grew again immediately, filling up the space I had emptied out till it became very large; then I operated on her inside her throat: she did not grow any larger after that. And I left those areas, only letting God do what came after me with this.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the inflammation reaches to the eye and it swells significantly and grows long, then it is called "perpendicular". And when it's swollen and spherical, it's referred to as "eye" or "uvea". When it has been cured in the way that we have described earlier, yet if the cure doesn't work and you notice that the swelling of the abscess subsides, the eye becomes tender, then it is time for you to perform a removal; and if it's round when gathered together and not long; and it's red or yellowish or black in color, it would be appropriate for you to avoid incision on this. Because there is great danger to the patient from this. So whenever you see it, based on what I have described concerning its brightness and length, you should make the patient face towards the sun, press his tongue with the instrument that we mentioned previously; then place an inch of rope into the eye and pull it out again while doing so; and once you've removed it to about half of a double thickness. And ensure that you remove only as much as necessary beyond its natural limit; because if you remove more than needed, this could cause injury to sight and speech. After incision, use what we have described concerning the incision on two almonds, and treat until she is healed. And should there be fear from the surgeon during removal, it would be appropriate for you to apply an instrument of cautery here. The manner of the cautery is liquid in nature. And let it so that his head reaches your health, then press his tongue with the tool we mentioned under the chapter on cautery, and mix it with live burning coal until not too thick or too clear; and use the movement of this instrument according to its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hair or part where we apply the medicine, like how a spoon moves, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the wound; and the patient remains still on his side so that saliva and moisture flow from their mouth into the medicine within, not descending to the throat and the neck; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the wound for half an hour's quantity, until you see the skin dry out and the actions of the medicine cease; and when you notice this, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, soak the cotton in the medicine, and place the instrument entirely covered with cotton above the cloth; continue to keep the cotton moistened over the wound as long as necessary; and do this repeatedly until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and heal after four days or five. And if you need to repeat the application of medicine cautery, do so, and after that, rub inside the wound with cotton dipped in butter, and clean out whatever remains within the medicine; and wash yourself with cold water, and continue gargling until fully recovered.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or the cautery method; if it's treated with fumigation following this manner, take calamus and rosemary, and oregano, and rue, and chamomile, and yarrow, and other similar herbs. Gather all of them into one pot or any of them alone in a single pot, place it in the pot, and bring to boil; ensure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot place one tool according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And use silver or sulfur, and let one of these be placed in the mouth for the patient until the vapor rises through their nostrils, allowing the wound to be burned; repeat this often, until the wound dries up, making sure you do not perform this at the beginning of pus formation as many things occur then; instead, only do this when pus is about to disappear. And if such a tool is unavailable, take one stick and place an eggshell in the mouth of the patient, so that their mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor weigh down on the mouth, and it's a good treatment combined with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it emerges in the throat bone or spinal column of fish, without anything else; therefore, if you must treat what you can see, press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument so that you can perceive any movement; and for what does not reveal itself to you, which is stuck in the throat, you should induce vomiting in the patient as if their food was cooked in the stomach; by chance if expel the obstruction through vomiting; or if the patient ingests a piece of sponge, a piece of navel, a lettuce root, or one small chunk of dry bread; and bind the sponge with one thread, then swallow it. And when it reaches its place, if it gets caught, and then pull forcefully; and if this does not work as what we have said, take one diving tool according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And have the instruments bent towards the head so that it may more lightly enter the throat, and raise the head high; and be cautious not to touch the epiglottis, that nothing might slip down or push the bone inside; and move when the patient pushes the instrument in, because if they are moving or obstruction is forced through; if it is pushed back down, or if it is pulled out forcefully with all the instrument evenly, until it is pulled out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No treatment is provided for bleeding from the nose, as I have explained in division through medicine cure. Should this not prove beneficial, then look into the patient's throat from where the ailment emanates when you press their tongue with the tool mentioned to you. And if you see blood within, guide it out completely or half an inch using a fine pair of tweezers suitable for this purpose. If that fails, take a weaved hair and place it in the throat from where the ailment arises; then immerse one end of the hair into cold water heated to a warm temperature, perform this several times, and let the water drip into their mouth until they can swallow it, moving it around frequently. And as soon as the patient senses the water, they will vomit blood.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it doesn't vomit as we have said, subfumigate the ailment with asafetida like we did in the fumigation of the eye using the tool mentioned for that purpose; do this several times because the ailment will expel without any fuss. The manner of the fumigation is such: you take one pot containing burning charcoal and place it covered in a lid halfway through, and there insert the tool's handle into the hole at the bottom; then blow your fumigation, and place the tip of the hair in the patient's mouth while closing their mouth, so that the smoke doesn't escape but goes all the way to the stomach; and now the stomach will expel. If it doesn't vomit, restart the fumigation several times; and let the patient drink, eat salty things or similar, don't drink water; and then it is necessary for her to expel forcefully through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat blood is like this: when one can see it, it resembles curved scissors meant for entering the throat; and it has a likeness to a doctor's beak, and it is sharpened with grinding, so that whatever she takes, she cannot leave it. And here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter concerning abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	The descriptions of abscesses are, according to what memory brings forward from one and the other in this book, and they vary in perforation and sizing; and there are two ways to do it, where one follows its own appearance and is moisture-related.
