And the second way is through the bones or where they are inside the body. because abscesses on the head are different from those on the foundation, and abscesses on the meaty part of a bone are different from those that come in joints, each has their judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And for abscesses one should not pierce them until the body is dead according to their maturation; and if there are such that it's necessary to pierce when they have grown, and do not die based on their maturation, like abscesses located in joints. For when abscesses come from joints, if you let them rot internally by chance, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint will become corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. Or if an abscess is inside the main member, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the main member; or if it's inside the foundation, piercing it should be done when it is dead; and it should not be allowed to pierce a growing abscess without complete digestion, except for that which is inside the foundation, so that it does not rot completely and remain buried within, leading to a fistula; and cannot heal in great extent.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of draining an abscess which is done according to completion, and this occurs when the pain subsides, and the departure of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and during the movement and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you keep the drainage hole as close as possible beneath the abscess, and where it opens outwards. And make the drainage hole long along the center line, and if the abscess is near the hands or feet, or at joints and in necks and arteries, and everywhere uniformly where there's no furrow.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that bend, according to the length of that limb. And when abscesses are in the soft flesh, if they swell you should leave the drainage hole until digestion is completed as part of the process, just as we have said. For if you pierce it before this point, pus would spill along with the body's venom and be filled with a heap of filth; and by chance harden the skin and the depths beneath him. And for every abscess that needs to be pierced according to the length of the body, as each limb requires. It is necessary to perform minor, shallow piercings, minor cuts; in larger abscesses, larger cuts, and many slits according to the size of the abscess; if it comes to such abscesses or one where you should shave him clean and cover; when he has healed as much as a small sheet, and is softened, then it must be done as it's done with sores: for those that are cut into three angles, and for those like the leaves of bay, like abscesses from angles; and for those where you make a round shape, and other cuts and similar shapes.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those that do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them thoroughly. And when the abscess is large, and has formed a big lump, if you pierce it, but don't drain all the pus in that moment, instead drain some part of it; then cover the abscess until another day, then leave no treatment for that period; do this step by step several times, until all the pus drains out. Similarly, when someone's strength is weak, or a pregnant woman, or small children, or old, decrepit individuals. For the body shudders each time with the release of pus, and by chance dies from the disease, and you wouldn't know it. Therefore, use this chapter cautiously. When you have pierced your abscesses, if there is a wound, check that the wound at the abscess site is small; and if it's a full cut, then apply linen or old cotton patches; and for large abscesses, and there are many cuts, then each should be covered by one patch so they stick together; and if you made a cut in the abscess into some skin, and sewed it internally, then fill it with old cotton or rags of linen without moisture, and bind until another day. Then apply, and treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your operation, cool water and ease are to be applied, and moisture for half a day. And if the bleeding persists, then take control of it and treat it, using the powders that I mentioned in this book, whether it is due to cold or when the place where you have inserted or opened has become very nervous, then it is necessary to put damp cloths and moist linens on it in wine and oil; and if it is in this condition, and the place is fleshed out, then it is necessary to apply damp cloths with water and oil, or in cold wine and oil for three days, as we have said; and then remove the dressing and clean the wound, according to how you should do so, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in treatments of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of these
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	From small pus discharges that occur in the head and are like in bandages, as with a worm's body, many seem similar. There are some fat and such which have moisture just like worms; there are also some that are hard like stones to a cutter, and there is no doubt they contain an artery without contradiction. And when cutting open for this purpose, use whatever tool called "entromissoire", as follows in its formation. It contains something because if it contains moisture, you do so from above over the long. And once the moisture is drained, then burn through without leaving any trace of the moist skin underneath, as it returns immediately when nothing is left behind; then plunge cotton into Egyptian ointment if available; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply this to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and that which remains overnight. And then resume with the cotton again as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know clearly it does not remain overnight; then heal the wound with ointment suitable for healing, until it is healthy. And if pus persists with one fat lump, cut along this shape, long; and let your cuts drain all around, and place your entire treatment cure over the bandage where it lies; and if the artery causes contradiction, do as I have told you after that. And also treat any hard pus bulge in a similar way, and when cutting and healing, as I have said to you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And when you cut into the hard pus and the wet area, it is lighter because there's little blood. If there are any of these pus bulges or shoulder joints where no moisture was found, as well as .i. (one) pus bulge that I copied from an old woman; and found the pus like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it. And if you had pierced none of them, you would have made cuts just as well as for one stone. In other pus bulges coming out or those coming from children's heads and ear roots, the opening should be left for as long as possible depending on each individual case, so that the bowels can come out; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	regarding the instructions for dealing with scrophula (also known as King's Evil or leprosy).
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times there emerges this abscess at the neck and in its vicinity, and also near angles, and nowhere else on the body or on any other organ; they are round, connected to each other. And each pock is properly within its bone, just as with the lymph nodes under the chin, as we have mentioned; and there are many appearances like these pocks. Some contain moisture, while others are malignant and do not obey healthiness. In that which you see has a good disposition towards treatment, and appears in the color of skin, silent from each side and not pressing against the collarbone or artery nor deeply; it is recommended to handle it from above, and scrape off each part, and place two fingers under each rib, if necessary as we have mentioned for abscesses under the chin; and treat gently and gently, be sure you do not cut the nerve or vein, and avoid excessive incisions that might cause bleeding, make sure your hands do not escape, and do not see too far ahead to avoid cutting what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it doesn't allow you to open further, place vitriol or some powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and restrain the wound; leave it until the abscess calms down and the wound softens, then begin to heal. And when the skin is healed, return to your work until you finish; then according to your skill's indication if there are still small pock marks, cut them out and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the pock, it would not be right for you to cut that pock mark at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread instead, let it fall off by itself without harm; then apply old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment to the wound, then begin treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire pock mark, it's necessary to assemble the two sides of the wound and stitch them together now, so that there is no excess left due to the size of the pock. It's necessary for you to be aware when cutting at its root, extracting fluids, and stitching as we have mentioned. Those pock marks held by excess, pierce where it opens naturally; and pierce in the same way as previously described, hanging down, then apply treatments with ointment and similar things, so that what remains from corruption is corrupted; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat with ointment until it heals properly, until it has recovered its health.
de squinance	Of squinching
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and discussed about the surgery of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squinching,[1] it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as "epiglottis" be made; and one should not attempt this, for all the veins and the lungs are vulnerable to illness in these who have abscesses either within their mouth or in the throat or .ij. amandines.[2]
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lungs, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we make a cut of three circles or four with one small incision through, between the two circles or according to the size of the incision therefrom, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those loops are suitable for the division of the epiglottis so there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough to reach it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to all inches, then cut through the knee until you reach the chain; and avoid any blood vessels, if you see anything, and then carve at this spot as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And this is demonstrated by the division of the canal of the bile duct that jumps out through the broken part of the body and due to the failure of the voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and keep the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed since one begins to doubt strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound as neatly as possible, and sew them all smoothly without the cartilage; then apply medicines that cause tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	All right, if you do not perform this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged as dead, and the defect remains.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	So protect the epiglottis because the patient can't breathe normally, and they are breathing through the wound, and thus is kept from dying.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And because they commanded the old man to leave the wound open until the illness's evil passes, and it has passed in three or four days or so.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to stitch the wound and clean it until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I see that a maiden took one knife, and stabbed it into her throat, severing some of the channels from the womb.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was summoned to treat her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found that blood was flowing from it, and indeed she did not have a cut vein or pathway leading out except for her throat, and the air entered through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, dressed the wound, and treated it until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And when the young maiden lost her voice due to this, she returned after recovering;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	For heaven knows that in tailoring the epiglottis, there is no need.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Thick abscesses are called "throat hernia", and they are large abscesses in the color of a grape, and occur very often in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And according to two ways: naturally, and accidents; or natural has no means.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to two ways, of which one is like fat in us, and the other way is like pus that comes from us through the artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it should not have fire done outside that in the one who is small, and prove and search throughout all the introducer:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as one small piece of fat, and cannot reach any vein, then do it, just like we do with us, and treat everything in its covering, if there is any doubt;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search carefully always, and treat them accordingly, until it is completely healed.
des nous	after us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways there are to do this, of which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is fitting that I should describe all the differences between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I state that the cause is heat and fever continuing until the boiling has passed, and the corruption is completed; therefore, the fever and heat must cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new one, there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains one gallbladder, which is its own sac and is within the flesh's color, beginning also like a cyst, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And according to two appearances, either fatty or moist, and most of the color are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the new one, that you first test and inquire about all the instrument which is called 'entromissoire', according to its form or chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of incising abscesses from us is that you take the wettest part you find inside the abscess and twist your thumbs gently, gently, until you know that the instruments have pierced the center,
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the pus, and take care that it doesn't jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture is found, whatever its color may be, cut as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the introduction there is no moisture, know that it's greasy, so cut it in a cross shape, and grab it with pincers, and lightly scrape off each side of it and remove the coat where it lies until you pull out the thing clean with the nut;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you can't pull it out clean, then pull it piece by piece so nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing is left behind, the issue will recur multiple times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it leaves a little behind and does not bother you, fill the wound with some corrosive powders and treat the wound, and place antiseptic things on hot bandages, and apply other treatments until it heals fully.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it is large for us, we measure two inches from the wound's edge, and prepare the treatment for the one who sutured the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is more than two inches against it or otherwise urgent, prepare and use the iron tool for a short time, leaving it in place for two or three days until the wound heals, then continue with the copper treatment that has been left over from the new one.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the instruments used for incision, and there are three ways: large, medium-sized, and small. If you have four squares which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb". And there are also three ways: large, medium-sized, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like needles from which one cuts the roots, and they are made of citrine crystal, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow in color are more effective than those with black polish to encircle the bends of fistulas;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the width of the cuts.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the hooks resemble sheep, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are two bends on the hooks in the same manner.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if there are hooks with two bends, they are also in these three ways; and if there are hooks with two bends and single hook that only has one bend, and they are also in these three ways; and all of this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tip of these is made sharp, and there are some that do not cut strength from one side only, which we scrape our hands with, because one does not sever the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these introductions have their replies placed on gloves, so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and only use the larger ones for places like the limbs, such as legs and arms, and breasts, and in similar body parts;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and no other instrument of one size smaller is ever made, resembling the bark of a walnut, with this shape, to which bleeding can be applied:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And we place it at once within its healthy location where all veins are properly connected, and with arteries, and in no way follow such grand form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	None of the males develop breast swelling as they start to become corrupt, until they seem like breasts of women.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to treat them, if it should happen to follow this form according to line b., up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and treat the wound with medicine that promotes healing tissue, then bring together the two edges of the wound for stitches, and continue treatment until it has healed completely;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the belly sags down, and is squashed by its size especially as it happens in women, so that she divides into two parts, with two similar cracks;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From which one supports the other at the end of each and both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b until this line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scald the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and follow what we have said about stitches and powders, and what is necessary for treatment until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it hasn't healed, or if the incision isn't fully made, because the patient doesn't want to rest or due to bleeding, you should fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment;
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it grow as long as it feels it, removing flesh and fat along with it, then treat until it becomes clean.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses and scabs
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from under the skin are manners of hard scrofula or when there are nodes, and if they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	So for those containing moisture, it should be cut according to this form, from line b. up until the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus from within the abscess is drained, one should fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until another day. Then remove all the cotton and apply balm to keep it clean until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles lymph nodes, one should open it as we have described for fissures of lymph nodes, and if the wound has pus, then apply a cautery in accordance with what we said previously.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn together, there are many times when abscesses form, and just as this happens with veins, there will be an incision made.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows this, then indeed when it is due to an artery, the abscesses are long and extend fully.

For when you treat them together, it's not enough to secure the head of the penis so that it doesn't pierce him, and brings blackness and corruption in his penis and the anus; if there must be cut away all that is black and corrupted, then cover with a plaster made of honey and flour which is made from almond skin and several times, then treat other treatments until he heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, it is necessary to use the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauterizing tools should be arranged in two positions together: that is, at the time of bleeding and during corruption; and if the head of the penis has become corrupted and removed, then it is necessary to use a darning needle on the penis and let the patient urinate between them; and when the hair is dry around the head of the penis which is at these who have never been circumcised, or there was injury or an abscess, then you should burn with one tool with four teeth, until all the ligaments are free and the head of the penis is released from everywhere.

And if it is hard to decide on this matter, then you should burn with two small needles near the head of the penis and the skin; then open nicely between them, and I place one thin piece of linen in cold water so that it does not dry right at the head.
de la circoncision	From circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely about continuation like other wounds; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our own will and specifically for children, it is necessary that we do the best job, and cause the least harm to health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old ones did not mention circumcision for their children, as they do not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz. The recipient receives treatment and experiences double pain. In the operation where the knife is halfway in, the point of the limb is not completely certain; and in the operation on a nail, by chance the iron escapes from the hole and runs through the work, and many times it grows like it should not require an operation, and this I have observed.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz. dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine

de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have discussed in our division the methods of stone extraction and amalgamation of medicines; and we explained the difference between stones that are removed surgically like kidneys, and all their signs, and on which stone one should perform a size operation; and about the bladder and penis; and I will explain it openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I state that the stone inside the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that there has been a urinary tract ailment similar to an internal one; it opens, and causes great pain for those afflicted, and they can perform many actions, after which it heals; and at times of these occurrences, the base becomes weak; and until the child reaches four years old, their recovery from illness is relatively easy, but is much more problematic in older individuals, particularly those transitioning between youth and age. And generally, the treatment for children with larger stones is easier compared to those with smaller ones.

de la piere des femmes	from the vagina of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes, the stone can become trapped in women and if this happens even once, it requires a cure. It is forbidden for three reasons: one possibility is that perhaps the woman was a virgin; and secondly, no one could find a married woman who knows how to protect herself from sight, especially when she is chaste.

de hernie carnouse	regarding fatty hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I never see anyone who dares to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And it was said by the old ones that this is done like a branch that is assembled in a way where you tie the veins, after trimming them gently above the fingers;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then follow me, and treat the abscess of the one who is working, as long as there are veins bleeding. And treat it in the way that we have said, until it becomes healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Never let the belly rupture in anger, as we have said, and open their insides; and do not allow any intestines to fall out except if it's because of a specific issue, for otherwise, it is rare. Fix everything continuously.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And even if they stay too long at this point, assume the wound or the abscess has formed, as long as the intestines are falling out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens through the extension of the syphac which is in the belly, as we have said, because it extends, then it softens and swells up their insides and opens.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and the treatment is by cauterization, as we have previously mentioned; and there are times when it's treated with iron in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and if the patient lies prone on their back between your hands, then lift the part that's swollen outward in a wide arc according to the size of three fists;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the fat that's under the skin where it follows, then take hold of it and place it on the outward protruding part of the fat.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and then press forward towards the belly, then cut the two protruding parts of the fat on the edge of the fat next to the middle of the fat, and cut both.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then extract the head of the rib, and do not cut it in half or extend the egg anywhere else, just as I have instructed you in treating the pineal gland of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then treat it by healing wounds. And when you cut the threads, if you remove and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The heart is confined, and does not show itself in the operation, and the cautery becomes wetted in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening the skin of the heels
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles in some men becomes soft due to the fluids within becoming softened and it can be observed; and when one wishes to treat them, one must make the patient relieve himself on his back, and let out the softened skin towards the natural skin. Then it is necessary that upon wishing to heal them, one frees up the discomfort on their back by removing the soft skin from three stitches or four firmly; then cut between the stitches, and sew the wound like any other injuries until it heals, and cuts the thread.
dou chastrement	of punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that chastremens is excluded in our law, and because of this I would prefer not to mention it in this book. And they are necessary only for two purposes: one being that the person understands when asked about them and knows how to treat them; and the other, since we often need to chastremen some animals to help us, such as with goats and sheep and cows and others. Therefore I say that chastremens is performed in two ways: either by attraction or through cutting.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites can be in two ways: one way is that between the two openings at their genitals they resemble a woman's natural figure, having hair and sometimes urinating there. And another way is for women, with something on their belly like a penis and two openings. The treatment of this type and female hermaphrodites is to connect all the parts properly, then treat them as other wounds; in the second type, from men whose urine jumps through the skin of the genitals, there's no treatment required.
de la tentigene	Of the measles
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Measles is an afflicting rash that appears on the natural body parts, it's so ugly to see; some women also have them as big as a hand, and this needs treatment. It's necessary for you to color the excess of measles on your hands or forearms, gently removing it; don't remove too much at once, in order to avoid bleeding, then treat with another method until it heals; there is another rash that appears near the mouth of the pregnant woman, she applies it and sometimes burns, resembling a cow's appearance, and for this they called it the old "cow disease". It must be treated as we have described measles and its treatment until it heals.
de erratique	Of cautery from fire command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratic is the one who fails to perceive the nature of the female body or has a small defect; it's natural either by birth or due to accidents resulting from disease; it can be caused by impurities in food, or due to subtle or coarse substances that are taken internally; and it results in symptoms being felt across the front, back, sides, or wherever it may be. Understanding this requires observing the womb and fetus. If the issues are superficially apparent, they might be near your hands or knees.
des emorroides	Regarding piles (hemorrhoids).
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Wounds are openings of veins which without customary treatment, and when wounds become hard, they turn into thorns; we've mentioned these aspects in section divisions, as well as signs, and I will now speak about those that respond to treatment. I state that wounds and the thorns, once they settle deep within flesh, cannot be detected by touch until they are treated with a metal rod. Those located at the opening of the wound can be felt, thus able for treatment. Hence, you should place the woman in a cold room, then apply the thorn using forceps; treat her roots afterwards, then powder with medicine that stops blood flow, such as comfrey and dragon's blood and incense, among similar items. Then bind her feet to her bed for an hour, then submerge her in cold water; should bleeding occur during this process, immerse her in a decoction of sumac, inner pomegranate rinds, and gall, among similar things, afterwards take barley flour, mix with honey and almond oil, make it into two plasters on her back. If it stops bleeding, that's good. Shouldn't work out, should she bleed from her back and nipples using force; then take sheep's wool, make a poultice of plantain juice or elderberry juice with old wine, heat this over fire to her. And when the abscess settles down, treat her flesh with ointment until it heals; one called 'albathir' is red, and resembles a hardened thumb nail, like thorns need to be treated similarly; then continue treating her until she's healed fully.
des apostemes de la marris	The contents of the wound
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many methods of abscess occur in the armpit, such as gangrene, stone abscesses, herpes, and other diseases that I mentioned in sections. Therefore, it is necessary to describe in this treatise on the hot abscess occurring in the armpit, which isn't one of the abscesses that heal with poultices; if you see the signs for iron treatment, observe whether the abscess becomes inflamed and full at the beginning of its appearance, and is filled with heat and fever, and if it turns red you can see it. Therefore, don't rush to pierce immediately; wait until the pain subsides; then have him lie on a single pillow, place two small pillows under his knees which he leans against, support his back and gather together his feet towards his legs; spread out his buttocks, place his arms under his knees, tie them well with a strong bandage; then bring up the armpit towards his right side, and apply the tool used to open the wound, the shape of which will be described later; it is necessary that when you see this tool applied, you make the first cut in order to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters the tool does not penetrate deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; if the tool is too large, then cover the depth of the wound with bandages, so the tool doesn't cause discomfort; it should have a funnel placed above the wound and cut the tool. And when the abscess opens, and you find it soft in hand, then apply to its head or sumpill hole; and once the pus is drained out, you must put oily bandages filled with oil roses into the wound; place the bandage at the depth of the wound, spread it under the wound and under the armpit with clean oily bandages that have been boiled in water or cooked with lily roots; then treat after two days with an ointment suitable for this, until it heals fully; and no time should be lifted the armpit and the wound by water and honey, and then water or lily roots long boiled; then revive with the ointment. If the wound has healed in the armpit, you should avoid iron treatment, but treat it as we said in sections.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The first profession in labor is recognizing the natural birth figure, and these are signs: when you see a woman rush to give birth, and desire to smell amniotic fluid: then the baby should quickly come forth; at this point you know that the birth process follows its natural course, and happens through her abdomen, followed by the second stage with it; and when you notice these signs, gently pressing her stomach is advisable so the baby comes out promptly; because as soon as it descends from its head, the second stage comes with it, and its placenta is born naturally cleaned of excess. Any other birth process does not occur naturally. It either occurs on its feet and involves parts of the body or limbs, or it involves her belly or breasts, and turns unexpectedly around its neck through other harmful positions; therefore, a midwife must be wise and astute in these matters and avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how to assist properly.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the baby descends through its head by a natural outlet, and the woman experiences severe labor pains, if her strength is weak, she should sit on a stool or have women hold her. She should eat food from fenugreek that has been cooked, and then have the midwife place between her fingers a small spoon (spatumile), as shown:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut the second part, and remove until the moisture that is within has left; and press on the woman's abdomen as the child descends, if it doesn't descend then you should administer castor oil to her along with fenugreek seed oil; afterwards have her take ginger and drink water, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: once the child is now out. And when both of those two hands come out forcefully, then gently insert them little by little; if they can't enter then put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then remove the stool from underneath her, and cut near the woman ensuring she doesn't urinate during this procedure; and if her hands still can't enter and the child has died, then take her hands with the knife previously mentioned, extract the child, and gently massage equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	from the birth of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	And when the child comes out on its feet, it is necessary to lift it up high;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn a little bit by little bit, until they are even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then hold one inch of the thread and extend it a little bit by little bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can he jump up to the thighs, if commanded, and make it emit smoke from consideration;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he can jump, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't adhere as we have said, if you twist a little bit by a little bit, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore, make it lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it doesn't follow as we have said, take a handful of alum, and oil of sesame, and ground gum, and grind all in one pestle until it is done.
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and apply this balm inside and outside the woman's body.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child takes this form, if you put your hands on it gently and gently.

et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And guide the child slowly; and instruct the woman to bear until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child which proceeds with one hand during

s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If one cannot bring it back, then make the woman lie down and walk around;

de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child at its neck, have it spread its arms, and twist its face towards its mother's back.

de l’enfant mort	of the dead child

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the wife to her place

de percier lou fondement	To pierce the base

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the base
