Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearances and the locations of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity in them is such that there are arrows with large points, and small ones, and those with feathers, and those glued;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And the one who urinates in no part of her body but according to two ways: or from a primary member, it pours out;
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	And when she urinates in no part of these organs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you need to perform the extraction of this arrow, because death comes later in various situations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when you don't notice this bad sign and the arrow hasn't been completely removed, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the brain sign when the arrow exits and pierces the bone, causing a gust of wind that is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	This occurs when blindness and numbness and vertigo are with us, along with a flushed face, and inflammation and red tongue, and spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps it affects the nose or ears; and by chance loses speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	It causes a moist white swelling resembling a boil in the wound, and also burns like burnt flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if you notice this sign, adhere to the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is still inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign for the arrow when it comes out or hits bone is that it's near the left mammary gland, and also feels as if it's embedded in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the vein may also become inactive like the hair, and in black blood, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	So, be aware that death follows with doubt.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never reveals itself is when there's no frothy discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with coldness.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow exits through the back of the thigh, it's below the small ribs; and there's intense bleeding and pain and sighing; and all limbs from the shoulders downwards move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach contents escape through the wound by chance, there is no matter of undigested meat in that.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach contents escape through the wound by chance, and there is nothing passing through the intestines in that jump, then there is no hope for treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow penetrates into the bladder and urine escapes by jump and leaves, causing great pain to the patient: know that this wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and shoulder blade and back spine and ribs and the legs, and seemingly similar limbs are safe according to various arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in your nerve or artery, and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you did something else.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened when someone shot an arrow at him in the left lung at the base of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and from another side across the fat of the ear, it was perfectly healed without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And he aimed an arrow that fell into the fatty tissue near the paper under the eye.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow had been returned, and one could not reach even its tip towards the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large as an Ottoman bow, about one and a half pounds without ears; the patient recovered, and he did not suffer any adverse events.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I pulled out the barbs, and after extracting them as I pulled, the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And shoot an arrow to one's half body, where it stuck or was embedded either in the chest or abdomen, and thought that they were dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after having passed thirty days, if it had not changed its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and attached a mechanism to it, and I forcefully pulled it out, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find that an arrow has fallen or been driven into one's back, and the wound has healed;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And allows the arrow to remain within, and does not restore its natural positions,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And for another man, who was struck in the face with an arrow, and had his wound stitched;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and then continued to endure great pain; and many others were similar.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And a spear was thrust for 1 home of the princes to the king, who had it stuck in his neck midst the battle.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was somewhat leaning towards the right side; and the spear was entirely upright.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called for the treatment after she had been pierced for three days. I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried all sorts of subtle tests on her, and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt a wound and pain all over his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on his head a plaster that absorbs and digests, because the ears were inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the tip of the arrow in the ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for several days, and resolved the wound quickly, then prolonged the patient's discomfort for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he felt the arrow within his nose; and I told him about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive mercury medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And I tried it out, and felt the tip of the arrow as it stuck in him;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then adjust during the opening of the wound through this blood-purifying medicine, until the head of the arrow becomes visibly apparent;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and make sure to reach deeply into the inner part for about four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then stretch it if the wound is too tight and I found the scissors were needed, and pull from both sides, but could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	so I kept trying to refine and devise ways of tools until I managed, on the second day, to use well-made scissors to extract it.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to how its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I am treating it, and will heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage under the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will do so then, and the wound shall be sealed, and completely healed of the malady.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Thus I have told you about the quality of extracting arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you place your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise masters compare well to a small amount of things, and on what is present and lacking;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find nine works, and the ninth instrument, for the removal of foreign objects that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are within the members where they are stuck according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	By the arm where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And the one that enters through an injury or where it goes in, it's an arrow entering the flesh, and there is no such thing anymore.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not leave now, let it stay until the wound heals internally, and expect its outcome.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly if it's stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let it stay like that for some days, and remove it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, if one pierces through all with a single fine needle, as long as the bones inside are widened, and then proceeds.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the shoulder, it goes up to one of the organs inside the head.
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the incidents I have mentioned become clear to the patient: if he does not remove it immediately, but leaves it until its effects diminish after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow has reached the heart, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only stuck within the bone, and does not pierce to its full length,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And let the patient rest for several days without any mishap, if the wound is treated properly.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's deeply embedded and can't come out, if you apply thorns internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has returned to within the body so that you can't see it, if one seeks for it with the whole effort;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, guide it to any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do it due to the tightness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is neither bone nor nerve or vein, cut it as long as the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears holding onto it,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If you extract a bone that is stuck at two places, remove it as far as you can reach.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrow's ears (feathers) until you can drain it completely;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	Do this skillfully so that you do not break the arrow, but drain it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't achieve this in one go, leave it until the arrow shaft is completely rotted, then remove it, as extraction requires agility.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding contravenes you, then apply what we have said about treatment in our chapter regarding bloodletting;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against cutting the nerve and vein, and apply as carefully as you can to extract the arrow without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or gently, firmly or clumsily; and guide the patient according to the form they were in when the arrow struck them,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because this is the greatest aid that you can provide, and if you cannot do so, place it according to what the symptoms show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or where it pierces anything inside him, or the skin is swollen in that place so you can see or feel it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then lift up, as long as the tongs can hold, and then stretch: if the arrow jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, let it still be there, and then start pulling it out again as long as it does not come out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if there is an arrow involved, hold it to the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it's bone, and you see it being administered by hammering, then apply a tool for that purpose.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the arrowhead enters into the groove of the tool; and then strike with force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is stuck in deep, use another tool with a pointed end to facilitate its extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, it's necessary for you to pull all the flesh inward around where it enters, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as seems appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow lodges in the leg or arm or abdomen or bladder or ribcage, and it's close to vital organs, and you can remove it, then lift it up; if you can remove it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to pull the vein and nerve with it, then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if that's what is required.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until she/he is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used for arrows resembles a bird's beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in various sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the needle's tip is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	In order to push against the tip of the arrow, as illustrated:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and retrieving is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common bodies
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From the veins from which we cleanse oneself are thirty-one, from which there is a head of sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is to know: two small things which are after the ears, they are called "the two grasses";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the corners of the two eyes, they are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that runs on the forehead; and the vein that is near the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two tendons which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above in the cheeks of the mouth, and these veins are called 'aughers';
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are along the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins by which we usually treat are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the occipital bone, and it's located on the left side of the head, and they call it the "blood vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called 'sawdust', and it's composed of the occipital bone and the basioccipital bone;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it 'the blood vein of the heart'; and the basioccipital bone is either on the left or right side of the head,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call this thing 'breath of the belly', and it is above the navel,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it refers to that which heals, whose opening becomes clearly visible at the scrotum.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the bloodletting tool is the vein located between the index finger and the ring finger, and if it's one inch long;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and below the knee are three veins: one is at the back of the thigh on the left side near the groin;
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And here comes the second sentence to translate.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins along those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears helps with the old plagues and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the healer, as I have told you, and that you heal the head with pain.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then pinch the patient's neck at its base.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	Until the two veins become visible behind the ears on both sides of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Place them then under your right hand, and where you feel the pulse under your right hand, touch gently;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the scalpel and place it just below the vein up to the bone, then raise your hand all the way above the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut and loosen the skin and the vein very carefully two inches deep through which to pass, and let blood flow out as long as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tighten and bind it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples serves as old grapevine grafting,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And so, and accustomed to surgery, and at the body of feverish tears for the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And that which makes the surgeon is just like what I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And when the patient strangles their throat until both veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse on both sides of your neck, and then judges by palpation;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the knife above the vein on top of your thumb, and hold the scalpel ready.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	And lift the vein at the top, and cut it, as you did in two other veins, and let out the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And after that form the vein again, and leave it until it has healed. We have discussed this along with their incision and extraction elsewhere, starting from this chapter.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment of the vein on the forehead is just as important as that of the frontal sinus in ancient diseases, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality is such that the diseases twist their necks, until the vein becomes visible.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the tool called a 'digger', whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another tool, allowing the blood to flow according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the neck to the patient, and tie the vein until it is healthy and no part of the operation has been done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Every time, it should not be that the flames are too strong; and the healing from the side, because the bone is close, and by chance the flames might break when they are subtle.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in two eyelids affects the eyes, and at the nose, and at the cheek, and in the ear at the earlobe, and to the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is such that the patient contracts their throat by twisting some string, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and make the healing passage through it, somewhat like the length of a flame, somewhat long, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle and accidentally break, then make correction with blood, as much as you need to, and then bind on cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein close to the nose is valued for fever, and sudden relief, and diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and likewise when it is old;

et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the fine flame long, and insert it into the lip in the space that is between the two noses,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well yet, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it burn too deeply below the skin, and bleed gently according to your need, then stop for a night as she heals very quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is how fire works:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two kidneys helps in tightening the arteries, and at the beginning of mixed diseases, and for various illnesses, and in edema, and corrosion, and herpes, and embolism.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of health is such that the patient's throat tightens around both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the masters remain at the head of the patient's illness, and the ill person lies for one day,

puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repeat the operation on the other vein, then release the knot, and gently restrain the veins halfway.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	So the advice is for those who have a condition to let their hair grow long and even; and if it starts pricking at its base when they are young, hold them in place so they don't move until they fully grow.
De la sainie des leivres	From cleansing of the lungs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of veins in the mouth helps to alleviate issues within the mouth, and leads to tooth decay, and gum infections, and cracks in lips, and dental pain and discomfort.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health is to make the sick person stand before you, and hold their neck back just as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left side,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them because they are black, and because in them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	now hold both of them, and if you do not know which one it is and you're uncertain,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you take the largest from each part, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, because it is a similar method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the healing of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins that are below the tongue assists after the healing of the head, and this is at the constriction of the throat, and with diseases of the eyelid, and with diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the healer is that when a patient's illness becomes evident under your hands in front of the sun, and you raise the tongue, and look underneath on each side there appears a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then heal both of them, do not overdo it too much, because near are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins in one's arm that are commonly healed are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	if you prick them with one flame for a long time, or with an olive stick if there's no knife handy, and they're called 'anisel';
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and fine according to the size and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the fire cautery is greatly renowned, and it is quite wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And one must open the veins full of large visible blood, and that contain large blood and disturbance;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the shape of the olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed in subtlety, and used for purifying veins in subtlety, or there is citrine subtle blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The treatment of a basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that affect the throat, and the collarbone, and the belly, and the chest;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is incumbent on the surgeon to treat carefully, and to be aware of the artery that is nearby.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he hits the artery, and bleeding occurs, then it is incumbent upon him to stop the bleeding, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And it should not be clamped with fire, but cut like a skilled butcher.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein is not clearly open, it is necessary for you to extract it, and change another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	You should not have any fear about this, or you can cut into its place instead of it, the vein opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And cut the artery before it swells up, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know how to find the location of the artery, it is necessary for you thus: when you are pulling on the arm, press as far as you can feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the place of injury, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein before it inflames.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And remember not to cut into the artery when you see the wound swelling up, because that's from the artery. Listen carefully then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulging up like a child's urine at the top, and the veins are red and delicate, know that this is from an artery: take care.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, place your finger for a while, and when the bleeding stops, that has happened many times;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	The person ties the arm, leaves it like this, and does not move it. And there is fear, and do not move until it becomes well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not bleeding, and it suits you, and the medicine does not reach you, if you need to open an artery, because the head of the blood retreats; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a bark of rue, cut it, take one half and bind it well up to the other joint;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound stops bleeding, that's good; if not, apply it as we have said, using powders that stop the blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the bandages are not often tightened excessively due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's connection.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The surgery in the middle assists that it treats blood from above the head and below the chest, and across.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because she is made up of the basilica and cephalic (parts), as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the surgeon to be aware of the nerve that is located there, and if it isn't too deep, and he finds the nerve;
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it inflates and health is affected, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it doesn't open in any parts due to its intricacy, then you must use the surgical tool beforehand; and listen for the nerve with your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The surgical treatment for the scalp helps, as it drains blood from the head, and aids with pain;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary for the surgeon to use the olive oil lamp or the myrtle balm lamp, because this is the safest of all veins, as it does not destroy the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Otherwise, it's necessary to try for the lightest weight and don't worry if one fails at first, just retry;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, some limbs might swell in certain individuals even when attempting for the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of surgery depends on your thought process.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about healing, it is that healing should be conducted only for the purpose of maintaining health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the healing take place through one of the three veins that are there: this means, the cephalic vein, the femoral vein, and the basilic vein;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And let healing begin at the beginning of prayers while kneeling, and in autumn and after meals during winter, when the sign of fullness appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And let healing begin on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing administered for illnesses does not have a set hour, but only when the need is daily or nutritional, at all hours and in all circumstances;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And nursing infants up to thirteen years is not advisable, nor pregnant women for more than a quarter of the months up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And one should not nurse the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when some wish to be nursed, in whatever way that might be, it is necessary for them to cleanse their intestines with a gentle enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there's much of urine retained, so that the vessels draw away from the intestines the superfluous matters harmful to the main parts;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One who is excessively fat from meat, or one who is drunk, as long as they are able-bodied, or those with dropsy,
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if after a colic passion, and vomiting, and stomach cramps, and frequent visits to the toilet by the woman, and from work, watching over things, and joining in activities, or when someone loses their vigor, or due to something from an injury or from physical labor;

puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then within or during bathing, if no obstacle is present, for purging of the blood,

et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and abstain that day from work, and pain, and excess, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be bound and seated, and let the bandages be higher than where you are being treated, and rub your arm twice or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then stretch halfway over it, because when it is too tight or too loose,
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the shoulder with your hands until the veins swell and you can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the wicks with a little old oil flame, then place your left hand's index finger on that vein above the shoulder a bit where you want to apply pressure;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein doesn't rupture or break upon being pressed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flow like strings when they're healthy, and there are others that are full of wind.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	yet if one places them over the flame, they draw to the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus one is of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, for in this situation one should have knowledge of such matters among the surgeons.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the veins open on the first try, it's good; but if not, you can still try again right there or at a slight distance from that spot or hastily, as long as the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limbs are swollen and the patients feel discomfort, let them rest for one or two days, and do not tie the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance pus will come out at the wound; do not go into water or bath, then restart the cleaning if it suits the patient;

et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And let the wound be elevated for a little while, in this way that the limbs swell; because this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb is inflamed, do not restart the healing process and apply a little oil instead, because it lightens the body's burden from blood, and heals in that area where the oil is placed.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus apply the oil-based remedy to each healing you do for veins, in order to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And similarly perform garlic and ginger with wine, when you place it on the limb; if the herbs are too strong they cause a lot of pain.

et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see something, place on any thing of aloes or of myrrh made into a juice from comfrey, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Many times pus and appearance would occur at the healing of the basilica: therefore place your hand there, and if you find the head soft upon applying pressure from your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So then you should not apply anything from what we have said, because by chance within that without the artery; but let it dry for one bandage to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is sound.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And lead each person to some blood according to the amount of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	But if their veins are black, let them bleed until it turns red; and if you see that they are large, let them bleed until they become subtle; and if it is too hot, let them cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it suits the one who is full and strong, needing blood extraction, to make him have a larger wound, and let the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it suits well to care gently yet often, and you must care by cutting across, not simply cutting straight.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this way of care saves from the bleeding out and constriction of nerves, and is better than a long cut compared to a wide one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body needs care in healing, you should give them moistened bread made from juice of quince apples; if they are feverish, then cool it with blood three times or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they have a cold constitution, eat moistened bread before the healing process in a syrup made with honey, or in an aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, ensuring it has a pleasant scent.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it fails in the healing process after a bit of blood, then it is necessary for them to inhale soup made from fat, and an aromatic subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have mentioned in the section or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to breathe with his arm and heal again, then when he is weakened by much healing, it should be that he heals little by little, according to the quantity of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to breathe with his arm after the first healing and has strong veins, then heal him 7 hours after the first healing or after the new hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if someone wishes to heal on another side, then one should heal the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood inside the body that has heated up, and it causes fever; so one must drain large quantities, and widen the wound until it discharges through the suture.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	After you have treated all aspects of healing, and place your hand on the heart when it heals, so that death does not come instead of the stitch.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	This occurs many times when the healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not right when you see a dislocation of the arm, and making blood flow out the second time, and if there are gaps present,
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, stretch out the arm quickly, for this would be badly done;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it until it heals the second time; or you should place the tip of the flame at the end of the wound, until the blood that was frozen in the gap flows out,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on one pinch of salt that has been dissolved in water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the artery has been cut, let it alone and do not compress it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the need is to drain blood a second time, then place the healthy one in its own location, or in another artery, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is made in such a way that it can be replaced by the main artery because of its composition.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of this treatment is that the patient immerses his hand in hot water, until the fingers turn red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then tie it somewhat moderately, so that you can see well inside, then now heal him/her through it, not too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And make them somewhat broad, and heal very close to the wrist joint, and do not let it go through, then put the hand in hot water, and allow the blood to flow with the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it's in this state, do not re-bake the hand in hot water, because you put it more in winter than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And healing from this vein is saved from all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of saving the right hand for all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Stretch the hand, and immerse it in hot water, until the vein appears, if you can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and when healing from the side, and if you hold it all over completely, so that nothing hurts;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too far around it either, because all the nerves are completely devoid of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And then place your hand in hot water, if there is freezing present at the wound site, it will not be able to escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, place an incision where there is a leak to seal it quickly, and then do this for each individual case.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health of his left hand is against the disease in the mouse [or perhaps 'the mouse organ'], and do everything as I have told you regarding the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The health of the stomach is against all diseases that are within the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	If it relates to diseases of the heart, and retention of flowers, and disease of kidneys, and old diseases of thighs and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its health is such that the patient bathes in hot water, and rubs their veins until they bleed.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and above the joint of the ankle; and the vein is at the ankle, and above that joint, it goes into many parts of the kidney;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Then it is healthy wherever it goes larger towards a kidney, or at the ankle, as long as it flows.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cure it on the foot, be aware of the nerves that are there, and heal through the middle just as when cutting a log; let the flames go ahead.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out, then place the foot in water and allow well for the vein to drain properly.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it heals the first time, then for the second attempt go slightly above it the second time because the legs are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about nerve damage, as we have said, and do the same treatment for the other leg equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The muscles of the sciatic vein are at the ankle's bone, and its health corresponds to the pain in the buttocks, when it is due to internal bleeding.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its health is such that the veins enter or swell, and they constrict above the ankle up to three inches by twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	but otherwise, the vein does not open; and if it does open, heal it in every way you can, and across it;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and take care to have it bandaged, for the muscles are bare, and it is very responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you can't find it, if there's no opening or pain in the front or back of the knee, and towards your little toe, be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And drain the blood as much as you see fit, and then release the knot, and place a cotton bandage over it and tighten; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Bloodletting with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or spiders, or leeches; and bloodletting can be done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction which can cause injury is done in two ways: it can be performed with any fire, or it requires fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and suction that is done by causing injury and through the extraction of blood can be performed using fourteen different methods in one's body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because some has it entirely around their head; and others has it deep into their neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the other two are in the two sides of the neck; and there is suction under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction of the two shoulders; and the suction over the pimples;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the suckers on the two arms; and the suckers on the two legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the suckers on the ankles; and suction therapy does not involve much blood, but rather small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and thus it does not weaken me at all, as we do for health of veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor with any fire or sense of heat, in any illness that comes from fullness, until all the bodies are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if suction is required due to illness necessity, or by custom, let us administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at its end, and continuously throughout every period.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to suction, weigh it heavily;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for such people, if they find fullness and redness on their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and they are troubled by these things;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have fainted, and are coughing up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are any such people who fear, see by the nose blood and noses and wounds and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed even during the last month, we instruct to fast after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The care of the mouth helps with the cold in the head ... where it comes from the eyes, and it is not right for this to happen after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this suction is in the place of the treatment of the occipital region,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it should not be used by those who have a cold constitution, or who suffer from catharsis, because to them it causes much harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, it should not be used by those who wear heavy clothing or suffer from cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And the one who often uses it becomes forgetful; for this reason, it is necessary to place the suction cup slightly lower by considering the risk of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventilation process near the neck is located at the place of healthy wind and the basilica, yet for this it benefits with compression on the foot.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and through the incision in the chest, immediately, and to replenish;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is better not to pinch too much, for if she holds too tightly, she may cause obstruction or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Ventilation at the two ribs near the neck helps with chest pain, eye disease and toothache, and in strangulation, and with pain in the roots of teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the location of the health of the basilica; and it behooves you to command the healer that he exposes his hand upon placing it, not to compress the artery, and not to let blood flow intermittently.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilation under the chin corresponds to mouth diseases and gum decay, and similar illnesses that occur in the mouth; it is related to the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders corresponds to sicknesses that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	Ventilation under the armpits is as important as three veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for she has bled from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the surgeon not to cut too close, for the artery is bare at its base, and lies beneath the skin and veins.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup on the back is suitable for bloodletting near the kidneys and internal illnesses. It's necessary that the suction cup be large and made of horn, as it needs to be handled well. By chance, if it were thin, it would break; and making such incisions causes great injuries.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs are applied openly because they drain blood from the entire body and are effective for old kidney pains, bladder issues, and uterine problems; they also help to weaken the body over time with prolonged use, leading to weakness in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method for applying the suction cup is to put it empty first, and apply a steady suck, then quickly place it, moving evenly, and keep doing this until you see the area turn red and swell. Once you perceive the reddish color of blood, then release, and replace the suction cups; be vigilant about the position of the parts involved, for some have thick flesh and clear pores: only one cut should be made in them, and large cuts with slight depth are to be done; suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the area is thick, it may require two cuts: the first one to delicately clear out the large blood vessel path.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very dense, it may require a third cut; and when we aim to draw out blood gradually and gradually, we only need to make one incision.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish not to have much blood, then we often begin again; and if the patient is faint, we give them strength, and the ends are such that the veins are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for those who have thick skin and hardness, and who have contracted sores, that you grease their ears with suction cups where an opening appears and a disintegrating agent:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the state of inflammation, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the form of pus, use rapeseed oil, or linden oil, or chamomile oil, or any similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of myrrh, or of balm, or aniseed oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one seeks to strengthen the flesh and large pores, there should be no need for any oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is suitable to wash after bloodletting with pink water, or cold water, or water from a rose, or water from a cucumber plant, or water from a porcelain dish, or other similar substances.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have much moisture, if they are lifted with help or with water from wormwood and sumac, and other similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses drink old wine, or water from vinegar, or decoctions of nettle or chamomile, or others alike;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and there is no cure of suction cup before or during the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and do not sleep afterwards during suction.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it should be noted when he is to be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And take care of those who are being treated if they are hot-tempered, and if their body is too active and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it requires cold things, such as apples of summer, endive leaves, lettuce, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And minced rabbits, and the meat of castrate animals, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with a cold constitution, they should consume syrup of honey and fragrant half-aged wine, which is between old and new wines, and eat small portions, and minced rabbits, and minced castrated animals, and young birds and chicks;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day he feels better, he should drink more than he eats.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no one men any thyme or muscatel before or after ventilation, or afterwards, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And season the broth well, but it is not good for him who sweats to drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed to irritate are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and in gout, and on the stomach and the intestines and the kidneys and the hip, because this member does not endure being irritated by needles.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and do it only to draw blood from one part of the body to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as when we place our hands on the nipples as soon as the child is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the body, as we apply suction cups on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the size of the body;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieve the pain, when there is an obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power it may relieve the obstruction, or remove the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way, when it is placed on the liver and the spleen if there is retained viscosity,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are used empty solely for drawing out fluid; and they are never applied together with fire, and not filled with water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	As in illnesses with weeping pain, and in such a manner that one fills the suction cup with hot water, or with water where herbs suitable for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup to be used on fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two and a half fingers wide in length, and at the center in the middle is an object of one small notch, like to pierce a needle,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and may be made of iron or silver so that it doesn't burn the patient upon placing it on the body;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And there is an inch long piece of a spider or iron rod in the middle, to place a candle on.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And for them big and small according to the illnesses and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suck-stickings for children are different from those of old people, and those for thin ones than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this suck-stick thus on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a candle wax plug or one inch long, and place it inside the suction cup at the tip of the penis which is within the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the heat remains in the bottom of the suction cup and does not burn the scrotum;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and hold it either at the part that we have mentioned, so that when desired, if there is a vapor, remove the suction cup;
