et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the paste in the same way as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup treatment for diseases of pleurisy, during all stages of fever, there should be neither too much nor too little fluid, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and placed solely on the body part.
et c’est li forme:	and it takes this shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction cups should not be applied except in parts of the body where it is possible to place suction cups due to their size limitations, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on the bare skin of wounds, such as arms or legs, and other similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of this user is that when you find nerves that are in sweet waters without infection, if you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And place them in sweet water until they become familiar and have nothing in their guts;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse the wound and use suction cups, after that rub the limb until it turns red, and place them on the nerves;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and start to hurt, if you can place suction cups there, do so, because this works very little afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift it with dry force first, and then with wet force, quite well, and afterwards apply the incision;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limbs are too stiff after the body of the surgery, moisten with .i. a linen cloth dipped in cold water, and place it on top, until the skin has turned red;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are multiple wounds, then place powdered vitriol or garlic and similar substances on top until the skin has turned red;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you place half of peeled beans on the wound, and leave them until they burn through the skin, which will stop the bleeding now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more skill, take other means.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins do not wish to open up, rub with a fresh blood source, or you insert an arrow until blood flows from it.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them, and as soon as they sense the blood, they start moving;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, powder a little aloes and ground wheat on them, or ash; they will start moving now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and in the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear boy, that the leaves of this chapter would have been lost from this book, had it not been found in any of the old books, nor had anyone ever read a letter from it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this reason, the knowledge has been lost in our land, for I have never found anyone good with it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And know this not from anything else, but solely by the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I applied the art in them, and through experimentation, and through my life's habit.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained here and summarized it at the end, clearly showing the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in those two chapters before this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to outline the contents of this book in our preface and specify the chapters where wisdom places its understanding, and remain faithful to truth. So that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twists or sprains occur to any part of the body, it is necessary for you to quickly tend to the patient from one side and the other, without causing them too much pain, especially in cases of weakness due to age, children, or elderly individuals;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the cautery is too tight or too cold; and consume cold joints, meaning cold jousts, and liver and buckthorn meat, do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with too many foods that fill the veins with blood until you have doubt of an abscess becoming hot, or spreading of matter in the limb. If the patient gets better under your first rule of treatment, which he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with meats that are rich in nutrients, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and peas, and pies, and veal liver, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And with this kind of nourishment, healing occurs more quickly and the break heals better.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken in old and weakened people cannot be properly set or sutured according to their nature due to the dryness of limbs, nor those also which are too tender, such as the bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but take care, reset the broken bone. i.e., apply firm pressure and join the limb together until it is as strong as before; and don't let him work too soon at his task, for this requires being nourished with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all about fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures going to an arrow wound, and others while sharpening, such as when cutting the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a fracture with injury, and a break due to a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each one has its tool, and its own instrument proper for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And one recognizes the fracture of the bone by how the limb is twisted, and opens well through it, and its sound when squeezed with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist or curvature at its end, and the patient does not feel significant pain, if there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have twists, or crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But it is not appropriate for you to move it with your hand, but apply the following remedies and then gradually constrain it now in a subtle way.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that was in the arm and the two parts are disjointed, now you should put them at the same level so that abscesses are applied on each side;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if pus appears, if he lets it be for any day, until the pus is calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then treat it equally with the means you can use gently and wisely, knowing that its restoration is easier than if there were pieces involved. Then apply, as follows.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are pieces in the bone, and it is split into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or near your hand for small limbs, or at two strings, or at one string and with your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the member are healed, you reattach all additions in their original places with means as you can, and remember that through your action do not bring about harm or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And properly adjust both ends of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it's not quite right: if the positioning is beautiful, and don't strain it too much, don't press as those who extract by their art do for pus discharge and muscle tension, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, restrain well the patient so they don't move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither upon turning, nor in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure that the limb is so secure that the patient does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, nor is it at ease, and he should be placed in such a position that he does not feel any pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him straight, so that no twisting occurs when he is being put back in place;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	the quality of the limb broken should be according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied in size and extent, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and alike; it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are larger, such as thighs and calves: it is necessary to wrap them with a wide and firm bandage; for wide bandages embrace the entire large limb, and constrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then place lighter bandages around them, either three or four times depending on the limb, and apply your hand a little to every part of the bandage, then move up past the wound and constrain it less, so that the wound can slightly separate from the skin;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage little by little until you cover a large part of the healthy area, then apply another layer of bandage and return to the wounded area again;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	After returning to the fracture area, it moderately restrains it, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have stated in the first instruction above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place linen strips or bandages over it until they are the same length, then tie everything up with one loop, and afterwards place your well-made stars on top. If there is no abscess or swelling, do this.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing on the area to reduce the swelling and alleviate the pain, and leave it for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then place something to hold the stars in place, and they should be half the width of a standard walking cane or sharpened to a point, or from wood used for making hammers, or palm leaves, and they should look like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	However, it is necessary for the emulsion that one places on the break to be a bit larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it fits according to the size of the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it on the emulsions just like you did in the first application, then tie an additional thread above it, similarly to what was done in the first application on the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	tighten this up slightly, not too tight; and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I want in works where they make their loops on linen cords twisted, and this is great mistake, because the loop cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it does not suit that there be less than two inches of space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the muscles are injured by the pressure of the shoulder pins after constriction in their healthy areas, then place them with linen or coarse woolen patches, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is under strain and the ribs are broken, I will say the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to forcibly stretch all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to apply braces immediately but only after five days or seven, or more according to your judgment of each new case occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of ancient plastering to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take corn that settles on mill walls, mix it with plenty of eggs, make this concoction neither too dry nor too thick, and use it. This is a common way of using plaster to restore fractures in various positions, as well as for women and small children, because it is neither too expensive nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations: take 3 egg whites, ladani, anise, asafetida, and gum arabic, each in quantity of .x. Z; myrrh and aloes, also each in quantity of .v. Z; garlic Z viij.; make this into a powder, then mix it with plenty of eggs; if the composition is hot, use this plaster because it has good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method for plastering in the case of twisting: take mugwort and valerian, each 3 parts; myrrh and aloes, each 8 parts; achillae 4 parts; boric acid from Armenia 10 parts. Grind these together well and mix with water or a generous amount of egg whites. Apply this preparation.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method for dressing broken joints and fractured bones, relieving the pain they cause, and aiding in their healing: take new wool, cook it with its grease and oil, and apply it on top of them. This bandage doesn't fully heal, but it is better to soothe abscesses quickly, and appropriately relieves bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for dressing broken bones that heals them: take dried fig leaves and earth-pine leaves, grind them together, and make a dressing.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way to apply plaster in restoring bone fracture and aiding the removal of pus. Take root of comfrey, chamomile, violet flowers, cornflour from each one part; grind it together, mix it with wine, and if your limbs are heated, mix it with coriander water or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method for applying plaster more forcefully than the first when pus has come to restore the member. Take roots of comfrey, and sesame seeds, balm, melilot, and winter savory, and violet and chamomile flowers from each one part; grind it together, mix it with salt water or sweet water or wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest period.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ippocrates states that one should apply on the broken member for restoration only a salve made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and asserts that it should be neither too soft nor too hard between two.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen suggests that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, things that are dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take mugwort and ome feathers or bird feathers, and sage, and equal parts of them, grind them together, make a plaster from it, and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then after a little while, take care so that the patient does not feel any pain and their bone in its place is not moving; if it doesn't dislocate by hand movements.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain occurs in the limb, or itching, no peace or swelling is felt, then hurry, and dislocate it again, and apply the plaster now; take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and dip it in water, and hold it over the area until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, moistened in water or oil of rose, and secure it with a bandage until you are sure of the presence of pus.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation subside in the limb, and alleviate the pain, then resume the gentle re-wrapping, and a bit of plaster, but do not bind it as tightly as before; and apply it with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus is discharging and turning red with pain and swelling, indicating an infection throughout, then you need to apply plaster and bandaging, so reapply it in the same manner as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if the limb does not show anything of what we have said and is not relieved even after three, four, five or seven days; and each time let it rest for twenty days, according to this, as long as there is swelling and until the joint begins to heal.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then keep the restraint longer than at first, and increase its flesh, as I said before; and if you see the skin dry more than it should, know that no scabs will come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then take the water that has come from it, every time you remove it, and let this happen once a day, and scrape off a little of the wound;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this work then cut off the scabs from the limb, and hasten what the foolish sight does, that restores the limb in a twisted manner: it is bad, and this makes the work useless, and I see nothing else but to rest and to open it straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	regarding various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures exist, and various forms, and their causes are assigned;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the neck bones crush all the bone up to the symphysis which is below the bone, like when using an axe or staff; for this reason, this type of fracture is called "axial fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword penetrates through the bone from above without piercing it, this type of fracture is called "complete" fracture; and both large and small wounds result from these two types of fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact or a crack or a fracture in the stone, or through a stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture present, which comes close to the ligament that surrounds the bone, or above the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that penetrates into the bone as finely as a hair, and this crack is small, and for this it is called a "hairline fracture".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made or caused by striking with stone, or falling, or by any similar thing, and causes a piece of bone to enter below, and they are so close together like when craftsmen work on vessels when they strike them onto the vessels; then the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	This happens more in those who have wet bones from their head, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And happens in all these ways of breaking, that small fragments are lost as with bones; and I will speak about this properly.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all ways of breakages by their diminution upon them, and the investigation in tests, and by the corroded flesh which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known through this: when one has revealed the bone and rubs it all around, if there is an opening of black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a breakage, beware of the illnesses associated with hair loss, and if you do not encounter any harmful incidents such as vomiting bile, mental confusion, extension, pallor, fever, and other symptoms appearing in various conditions, there should be no doubt about recovery.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming incident, yet still hope for recovery, begin your treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the first snow comes to you, and it's winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the snow starts.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's winter, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that pus forms under the bone and the incidents we've mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone breaks until it reaches the membrane covering the brain, you should split the broken part like this: take hold of the edge of the bone in your hand and expose it completely on the surface of the bone using any method possible, and especially exposing as much of the wound's appearance as possible.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood flow is required to reveal the bone or pus pocket, assist with what is necessary and use wet cloths filled with rose oil to fill the cavity;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the pus pockets are calmed and there is assurance of blood flow; then begin inside towards the bone to remove, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut in a narrow line in front, and this forms:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then use another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different sizes of cuts, some narrow and others wide, they should be pointed, and made of metal; and apply them lightly to the work so as not to pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it should be pierced through (from both sides), so that cuts are made with needles, not completely through until they pierce beyond the bone at the tip, and there should be a margin or a circle above the point, which doesn't let the tip pass beyond the bone; and you need more than one, so that each goes to its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have needles for all sides; and this is the shape of the three methods of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the broken bone is that you place one needle on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then put the needle in another spot a bit after, and do this throughout, then carve out the distance of the bone which is between the breaks using incisors, as finely as you can, and gently, just like we said, so long as you are able to remove the bone with your hand or any tool you have such as forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is fitting to reset the preparation that has remained of the bone with all one instrument similar to a canine tooth, but it must be thicker and more delicate than another canine tooth;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, gently remove them with one instrument. Then heal the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this which Galien stated, which is safer; and the force is very much, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone where the break opens outwards, so that once you have uncovered that part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision tool, which is its shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side, and have the part divided into two ribs, so that when you are cutting you are towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, such that you gently touch the entire bone, and be well aware of the cloth that is nearby;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it's pressed against the bone, gently do so because you can feel the bone without causing harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks without piercing through the cloth, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces left, then after that abrasion, use the subtle scraper to remove scales. You should have various quantities of this tool so you can provide the most suitable treatment for each area according to the workpiece and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you stand before many rough judges, and then even more subtle ones, and never stop doing this until it's done properly.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other's haircut trimming and subtle breaking, it is necessary that you adjust according to their orientation; this thing cannot be answered by the one who has devoted his studies to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sinew is discovered, it is necessary that you take 1.25 drams of linen cloth according to the size of the wound, mix it with oil rose, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another piece of double linen cloth and soak it in wine and oil rose, then place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can so as not to weigh down the sinew, then apply another layer of thread above it without pulling it too tight that it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let it be like this for one or two days until the abscesses subside, then dislocate, and administer remedies such as root of garlic, flour of cloves, incense powder, and aristologue, and similar things; from these make a powder, put it on the wound, and immediately after apply medicinal powders without causing irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure that the wound is thoroughly clean, do not leave any ointment there nor allow bandages to stick too firmly together. For when bandages stick together under the brain's cloth, they can spread and cause great harm to the patient; for if one applies something irritating above it, it causes irritation from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take care, should any unfortunate events happen to the patient as we have described, if it remains uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if noor does not come out only because of the medicine we have put on, and if that virtue exists, then it is necessary for you to take a part of honey, and three parts of rosy oil, and one spoonful in glue, and then apply it onto your skin;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then follow the ways of healing as it should be until they heal.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts below the nose are ever broken or only one by itself, because these are two bones; and this lower part is cartilaginous, it does not break, nor should you twist or bend it, then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you bend your small toe or press against the nose, and set this break evenly within your index finger, and outwards towards the tip, until the nose revives according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain through your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and cannot reach to the nostrils, you should place it level with the tip of a small stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, then remake the splint, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess is pacified, then apply to the head of the nose a bolster made of linen bandages, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you apply heat from another source on the other side, if breaking occurs; and make the attempts so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And say that we must moisten the attempts with butter and change each day. I don't think this is quite right, but it seems better to moisten them in preparation for an egg broth and powders from a mill; then leave the attempt until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And whenever you use goose feathers in lieu of attempts, and if you have one egg broth all around, and the wound stays intact, and blows on the patient from within; do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose as you're working on them, then put in a wad of moistened cotton or balsam-soaked cloth, or a pinch of wormwood oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the abscess is not present, then apply a plaster outside, made from sawdust powder and incense powder, mixed with beaten egg yolk. Then place it on light bandages, do not tie them too tight.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture is small and it breaks into small pieces, then use suitable tools for this purpose to extract them. Then open the wound, cleanse with things that burn away flesh, and stitch, using plasters and ointments suitable for this task;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no injury within the nose, then perform the treatment, and place flax on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured inside and there's no wound on the surface, and only the breakage is outwardly present, not broken into two pieces just inside, but rather like a fracture within, one can easily detect it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you bend your index finger into the mouth towards the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, then bend your right hand's index finger instead, apply gentle pressure to the fracture internally, and move it with the other hand outwardly, ensuring equal force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is dislocation of the jaw bones in two places, it's necessary to provide an extension of both parts until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or a rupture, then stretch them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk. Then place on the broken mandible wadding, and put on one piece of double cloth; and put on this cloth a large wedge well made, or a piece of leather equal in size, long and wide according to the mandible, and fasten it there as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest. And have them eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then readjust what has changed; apply plaster, mix it with powder from the mill along with plenty of egg or almond flour after you have removed the wadding; spread a light woolen fabric over this plaster. If the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change, leave them as they are until they recover; many times recovery occurs within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if it comes to incisions or wounds that require dressing, you should carry out what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a breakage and wound together, reward none of the bone piece in has been removed; so delicacy is needed for using tools suitable to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains none, if the wound is large, place one dressing suitable for this on it to encourage growth until it heals.
de la forcele	by force of necessity
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strength is broken many times in front of the shoulder joint, and breaking occurs in three ways:
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedures are as follows when there is a breakage that occurs with injury: you need two assistants, so one can mark where the shoulder joint has broken and feels the broken strength; while the other extends their neck towards the affected area. Then place the breakage evenly on your hands, so it forms correctly and lacks any appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round piece of cloth or wool under the shoulder towards the leg; make its size according to your needs. Stretch and lift up the strength, hold the ball in your hand so that you can evenly place the breakage as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force by force outside, because it comes forward, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their back with their shoulder, and place a half-sized pillow under the shoulder. Then have someone support the shoulder downwards until the bone of the force is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the crushing to your thumbs, and if you find any debris inside, it is necessary to cut through; and gently pull the pieces apart. If the bone cannot join under any pressure, cut at one of the incisors that you have made. But when using this tool on the force, place it near so as not to miss it:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	It should resemble a spoon, it is not to be placed too close, and it should be as wide as necessary, depending on the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two ends, just as you see, and make one broad, and the other narrow, just like the wound you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the presence of pus, if you clean the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt about pus being present, then cover the wound with bandages and tents according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And when pus comes out, if there is moisture, spread oil of roses, and alcohol, and wine, and place them on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The dressing of the bone, when it involves wounds and cutting, is to apply a plaster made from ground powder and yolk of egg on the bone, and place light cloths on top. If necessary, put a ball under the wound area.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large band about the size of a palm wide, and place two layers of cloth on top of the plaster, then add more plaster. Next, take an elastic strip about three fingers wide and long, wrap it around this band, ensuring that the ends are hanging down from the band.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And place the cauterizing tool on the burn area, and turn the metal stick towards the neck, and around the healthy wound, and around the diseased wound; and reset it in each section, and when you see that the healing takes hold of the burn addition, and you clearly see that the cauterizing tool does not move above the broken bone, then reward it daily, and when the ligament is removed, then restrain it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	Let the disease heal on his back, and place him when he sleeps in a small pillow under the wound to raise the shoulder; this will ease the pain from the broken bone due to the positioning of the shoulder blade. If you can lift the dislocated shoulder by aligning it properly, or if you tie his arm around the neck, do not let any harmful accidents happen until twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then restart the plastering if you see it needs more, and hold it in place as it is until recovery occurs. It should be fully recovered by twenty-six to thirty days at most, with no exceptions for any individuals.
de la brisure de l’espaule	On the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or moves out far from its place, or it is dislocated only halfway; if this happens through contact; then treat according to the shape of the breakage, and reset accordingly in its natural form. Do so in all possible ways that you can. Then apply with coarse mill powder mixed with plenty of eggs, and gently tap until done. Apply two layers of cloth. Then place a large but slender pillar, slightly wider than the shoulder; ensure there is no disturbance around the shoulder area. Cover this with strips of linen, making sure the pillar fits evenly; then tightly bind everything into a large firm bandage so that the pillar doesn't move from its place. Check the binding every day; and each time it loosens, tighten again, ensuring the pillar stays in place even if it feels loose, and has the patient lie on their side. The shoulder is restored within 20 days or 25.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut. de la brisure dou pis	Of the breaking of the heel
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The feet are sometimes broken in the middle but this happens rarely; they often break at the front. And when it is broken in the middle, if you lift it up, there will be pain felt down below, and lack of circulation, and nausea, and sometimes vomiting blood, and it opens the movement inside the broken bone, and one feels well the situation.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for restoration, if the patient is lying on his back, you should place him on his side, then press down with your shoulders, and join the ribs of both sides using your hands, and carefully put them into equal positions as you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then lay over plaster casts above this delicate salt mold or another light substance, cover it with one cloth, and wrap it around the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn back to his front side, adjust carefully, and every hour apply pressure on the wound, if it heals it will tighten further; and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion, itchiness, pain or pus coming out of the wound, do it quickly and release him, remove the plaster, treat according to how you would for such conditions; then reapply the plaster until healed.
de la brisure des costes	From the breaking of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs happens only after the back muscles and inside the head, it does not break due to anything else; and one feels this well during examination in the court.

Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break in the ribs is deep inside, the patient will feel extreme pain and sharpness, like weeping, because the bone touches the lining; they get blisters, and all over and immediately vomit large amounts of blood, it's a painful illness, and the old ones have put great effort into recovery.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if someone says that it is necessary to eat meats which swell the belly, in order to relieve the windiness outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not follow this advice, that pus and worms do not arise without having already been there.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come about, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And let no one amongst us use suction cups on the body to suck out matter, because it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the suction cup draws away excess through the weakness of position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine. And if the wounds feel great pain that cannot be borne by the bone piercing the skin, there is doubt in the patient whether to cut through the body of broken rib and whether it's necessary to place a tool under the wound; then you must cut into the bone, drain gently, and then stitch together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until healed. de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No fracture occurs at the neck's bones, and it does not bend; similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to no one, and you want to know whether it will heal or not, if you see that his hands are softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if he does not sense anything. Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if such accidents do not come to him, it is a simpler thing.

And the treatment is: if there is an abscess to drain, you do so; if it's inflamed, apply oil or egg yolk on the spine or on the spot; until the inflammation subsides. Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is fractured, it must be covered with a poultice of its own nature; remove the bone, then join together the two edges of the wound if they are large, using stitches if necessary, then treat with an ointment that binds and heals until you feel better; and if there's a fragment from the bone, which is called 'the chip of the knee', hold your left hand pouch against it and place it evenly on your right hand at your power, then apply the plaster and elevating it as needed. Then compress it; and if any broken bone needs to be done so, do it upwards, remove the bone, and treat the wound until it heals completely.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the breaking of the bone in the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the hip bone breaks, and when it does, if there is a little pain in the head; and it stretches long, and declines to the kidneys, and comes with pain in the limb, and bruising, and swells up what is broken.

And the restoration is that you extend your hand upwards as long as you are at the breakage; and know where the breakage and its shape are; and if the breakage is only in the head, place an equal break there until it reaches its natural shape.

And if the abscesses burst out, do not touch them until the abscesses are soothed, and place them as we have instructed previously. de la brisure de l’ajutoire	from breaking the splint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The aids are those between the arm and shoulder's head, if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of these two ways: where one way involves taking a single medium-sized stick, in this manner:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie as two sticks together, and place them upwards, and bind the wound on one spot; then lay your broken arm onto the stick until it reaches the elbow, holding halfway with the stick's curvature. Then position anything or have assistants hold it from below; next, place the torn skin evenly between their hands as long as the torn skin returns to its original shape as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one binds the wound on their shoulder blade, and ties the hand to the neck, then instructs two assistants for each side that one shaves where the torn skin is at their hands, and the other shaves around completely up to the middle of both sticks, extending each person to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, hold one ligature over the wound and above it, spreading each minister to their part. And if the wound is close to the head of the shoulder, it is necessary to place one ligature halfway under the joint, and another towards the knife, under the wound; and similarly if the wound is facing the knife, it should be necessary to place a light ligature without effort, as long as the wound is even above the top and above the knife; then make an even incision, according to need, and hold, so that no pus comes out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if pus starts coming out, do not tighten it for up to seven days, and place it on greased linen or in oil, as long as the pus coming out is calmed; then tighten, and use this method of tightening: when you put plaster on the incision, then assemble the arm over the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; apply the bandage, and tighten it on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm stays in its usual position, without anything preventing it, or if the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use braces, and place a larger and stronger brace over the incision than the others, with one inch of space between each brace. Make sure each brace is large enough to pass the wound by about three inches on either side; then tighten them according to how I explained at the start of this chapter regarding wounds, more firmly but not by pulling away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the place where the bones meet and their constriction, as we have said, in your first attempt to restore the broken limb, and if you are uncertain about discharging pus (as an incision might be needed), then leave it bound for seven days, as we have said. Then check each day over three days on this tie-up, making sure no itching or swelling occurs around the limb, or that any complications cannot reach the limb because it is too constricted. If you notice anything amiss, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such incidents occur, or if it is released only after two days or more, and the patient remains in bed with his hands on his stomach; and place under him one cushion filled equally with cloth, and observe each hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or that the bandages are no longer moist. If this happens through the virtue of medicine, and he regains the flesh we have placed before, in such a way that the meat becomes tender; and when it starts to heal, if it is large. And it is customary for the shoulder and leg should be replaced within forty days from start to finish; and then you must release him and administer baths and medicines of ointments for his recovery. If the constriction is ugly or tangled, then he must remain in bed for two more days or a month.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones which are called the pair of 'fosciles', from which one is small, it is the bone that supports the pit; and the other is large, and it is the bone located underneath, towards the little elbow; suppose only the larger foscile breaks or perhaps the smaller one, and suppose they come together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fosciles break, restoration is light and healing; and when the large ones break, the healing becomes ill-fated, and worse than if they had broken together. If it's only the small foscile that breaks, then a slight extension should be suitable and made equal.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large foscile that breaks, then you should strain harder; and extend over one cushion, and raise the hand's pit higher than the others, and make the small bones lower than the others' bones, and ensure that the patient's side is crisscrossed with him alone, and another cushion above him so high that his side does not suffer any discomfort. Then extend your assistants' arms towards the part under their hands or at one elbow, and another assistant at one arm above. And then place the bed perfectly flat according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.
