And if in the break into pieces, you place each in its location; and if there's none that sticks to one of them when you grab it by the heel, then you can't restore it to its place. So do surgery on it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if in the case of injury that leads to a wound, I've mentioned this specifically in another chapter; take the treatment for it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the beginning of the restoration process, there are pus clots present, then coat .i. with a wad made of rosin and white beeswax; ensure it is neither too hard nor too soft. Bind this wad gently above delicately until the pus clots have been calmed. Then remove the rosin, and apply the plaster containing ground powder from a mill mixed with enough egg, place the needles, ensuring they are positioned closer to the injury at first than elsewhere; make sure there should be seven or eight needles in various positions: whether the injury is within one bone, two bones; bind more above the injury compared to other places, following what I've said at the start of this chapter; ensure that the cloths covering the injury are moist and soft, not too hard nor abrasive. Use threads made from linen that are neither too thick nor too thin, as we have discussed. And keep up with re-bandaging the limb and joints for several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any unfortunate events come to the limb, for example itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you immerse the limb in hot water until the itch is relieved; and let the limb not be forcibly restrained. And then begin tightening again, and when the bandage is undone and the bone is exposed, and something like this happens, direct your efforts towards resetting it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if one takes care that no injuries can occur to the limb because it is too constrained, it's necessary to soften it with a poultice, and leave thus for some days, until the pains subside, and then retighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, or if the loosening lasts up to twenty days or more. Or else after this time, then put his hands on his neck, and make sure both sides are equal, and beware of movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this strain is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and by chance in twenty days, according to the compositions and the complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and in its knuckles there are few injuries, and they only bend many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to keep their fingers together and straight in front of them equally; then place their hand on an extended surface, and extend the fingers of the broken bone, placing them evenly side by side until they are well aligned. And put a plaster and bandages, if no abscess forms, then place an elastic band according to the size of the hand; and wrap it in one linen fold.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is in the inner part near the belly of the hand's sole, make a ring out of linen and tell the patient to place it on their broken heel; and then stretch it with a long piece of linen, and have the band wrap around as well as can be, just like how big the hand's sole is, and stretch it, according to what fits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the breakage is at the front, it is necessary that you place one support above and another below on the heel, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie everything together throughout the hand, and seal the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the breakage occurs on any of the fingers, it's essential that you treat them equally, just as is proper; and restrain with the heel, and should you see if placing a small upright support helps to lift the breakage, and doesn't move; and if the breakage is in another finger, like in the index or one of the others, do the same, and tie it using the healthy one that follows; or tie them all together with a single band, until you can properly treat it, or place a support similarly, as we hold them. Pay attention to the restoration and arrangement of each wound separately, and take care of those who come before you, just as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken foot
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see this when it turns in front and behind; and its restoration thus consists: i. the joining above the breakage, and ii. another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And in the patient's abdomen, then extend each minister his link to its equal part; and this is when the break has entered into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, then one link goes towards the knee and the other links go under the breakage. Similarly, if it's near the knee, then place the ligaments below the knee, and the extension downwards; then set the eye of the bone equally with its two hands, as long as it follows its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the link, if pus doesn't come out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess to be treated with cautery, let it heal before you return to your work and treatment; the incision is made in such manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you cover the wound .i. with a bandage made of two layers or three, and keep any excess, then lift your leg so that the heel reaches to the root of the thigh, and insert one thread long between the knee and the leg, underneath the kneecap, and tie this thread at the top; then cover the wound with this, and place an end over the bone in the leg; then insert a piece of eight inches between the leg and the knee from the cloth to evenly apply pressure, then begin to bind firmly .iij. or iiij. times around the wound; and as you go beyond the wound, tighten less; then take two pieces of thread that you have inserted between the leg and the knee, and tie these three pieces over the wound area starting from underneath until you reach below the foot; and tighten it so that it doesn't move in its place, then leave it like this, and wait for no other sign such as pus or inflammation.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, loosen the binding and address what has occurred, just as we have said many times. And if there are pieces of bone that are being gripped, if it is possible to cut them off, do so; and if you can't, it's appropriate to cut through the cloth and drain out force (hemorrhage); and treat it in the way we've described, until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And not once is the flesh broken like when we insert needles, such as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, no complaint comes from the patient during this kind of restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the flesh is restored in one week, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the knee joint there is little breaking but it bends many times. And if it does break, it's usually just a crack or half an inch (one Roman inch) of separation and can occur with or without injury; one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is this: you should put in equal what was removed from its place until it can move freely again when assembled. Then apply plaster and add a round splint if necessary, then adjust as needed. Proceed with all the preparations we have described for other fractures, such as abscesses or similar occurrences. For each situation, apply what suits that particular case while maintaining soundness.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You know that the leg has two bones. One of these is named 'right' as 'mustelz', and the other is called 'foscile'. And any sort of injury or breakage can happen to it just like on the arm, and for this reason, the process of restoring a broken leg is similar to that of an arm, and all the techniques are exactly one.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn towards the front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bones are broken, one feels great pain and sees it clearly; then turn around. So apply extension, make them equal, and tie the ligaments equally; however, when the breakage is obvious and there are multiple fragments, the extension should be less intense and more gentle; and support them according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two furs of horse hair that strengthen the leg on both sides, and they should be as long as the length of the leg from the knee to here. Then wrap them in two strips each over and under it, and tie them in the middle, so the leg cannot bend either right or left, and thus it is well; and no one administers a bandage that is as long as the leg, made of fur, and they place the leg to ward off movement, and this must be done precisely where there was injury; and move the leg every day to see if there are any signs of an abscess or other accident; treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the breaking of bones due to injury
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	Ankle injuries do not come from breaking, but in bones due to injury there is a break sometimes and the bones themselves, only distress occurs in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there occurs a break in the bones due to injury, and you see these bones mount over one another, place such wounds on the ground like they would want to go, also as it were. Then put your foot on his foot at that point where the bones are raised, press them so much that their life returns; then put the plastering materials in the middle, cover them up, and place a small table under the belly of the foot with two shoulder-width planks, then bind them to the foot's inner side. Finally, wrap cloths around them or other things you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if you release the bandage, because you will find the bones even, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the ribs are broken, mend them, as we have said for the ribs of the hand; then place upon the broken rib an elyptical piece according to the length of the rib, and slightly larger, then put under it the table I mentioned, and tighten the attachment; and if there are two or three, or more, break them, if on each rib you place an elyptical piece according to its size, wrapped in one linen sheet, and tighten the table under this piece; and stay positioned on the top of the table facing down towards the belly beneath it, so that it cuts well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things I've said about other injuries, once we have discussed them; and treat each case according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of her nature is broken, she must be made to sit larger, then incline her towards the lower part of her back, and hold her by behind; next fill up the space in her nature with cotton, and place some as big as a thumb inside it; then get her up again and lift her bottom little by little, and when she has jumped off the cotton until it reaches to the entrance of her natural opening, and the bone returns with the thumb; and when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and once she has done so, put her back in position and do this for seven days or so: if there is healing, take a goat bladder, tie a stick to its mouth, fill the bladder entirely inside her natural opening; then blow into the stick strongly until the bladder swells up internally: nature will restore the breakage; after that fill it with cotton and leave her like this for some more days, until she has recovered.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the hand is broken, or that of a woman, if it's restored in this manner as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures should not be ignored by those who study and use them, and read my book. For the breakage signifies through multiple positions the right path to restoration: hence understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an oxtail and fill it with the penis; then wrap it in bandages all around, and leave it for three days or as long thereafter, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, even if it's large, such as the bone of the rib or shoulder or resembling others, that it should be now cauterized, so that the cauterizations which we have mentioned testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, you should still apply vinegar to it, even if you don't have anything else. Proceed then to restore the break in the same hour or day, or at least wait for the pus from an abscess not to come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if pus from an abscess has come out, allow the restoration to continue for another day or two, until the pus subsides. Don't touch it at all on the third day or fourth day, as you might provoke a bad setback.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if you see the bone broken appearing on the part uncovered by the cut, it is necessary that you place your hands gently on it, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not appear for you to place evenly with your hands, then take this tool made of iron, which is about seven inches or six inches long, and its width should be according to the size of the wound; and it's necessary for the surgeon that he uses three or four of them, depending on what he needs for each cure of broken bones; and may be round and a little thick so that they do not bend under compression on your limb during surgery, and may be smooth in front, and thick at the center advancing, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche" for that reason, so the curved bones should be placed on top of the visible part of the bone; and strike once with it, until it returns, and make them even against each other. And if the breakage is subtle, and the tools cannot properly grasp the bone well, then you must hold the tip of the bone as long as the tools can have possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone, as we have said, using an appropriate tool for this purpose, such as an incisor or saw, with your power; then cut that which is remaining in the hard and small scratches of the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. Do as much as possible to make sure it's in its right place, then apply once or twice with a black stenchy ointment, and properly if it’s in this state; and do not put anything like wax or other things where there is inflammation, so that no putrefaction or corruption comes about; then give these remedies after you have restored the bone, and let the wound be open, and cover it entirely according to the size of the wound, and make sure that the wound is not strained with breaking; and many times this has been done by fools, causing death or corrosion on the patient once; and let your compresses be softer and more soothing than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you suspect that harmful incidents may occur there, as we have said, and you find pain in your bones, then it's not appropriate to apply these remedies; but wrap it completely instead of applying them, with hard cloths and secure them. And when you see after one day or two days an improvement at the wound, remove whatever you placed on it entirely in wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as the tetracycline ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be braced in such a way that the joint moves slightly backwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot be joined back but allows movement of the joint, you should know that there are small bone fragments causing this pain, so it is necessary for you to treat the wound with traction, and remove all these worn-out pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula occurs at the site or in another way of corruption, you must treat it according to what was instructed in his chapter before. And when bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the bone of the shin or shoulder blade, or other similar large bones, do not treat it because death often follows; but let it heal until it turns green; perhaps discharge from it after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The blows that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The blows come often after the healing of injuries, even especially when close to joints. It's a thing to see how the member's shape changes; and by chance can't perform its natural tasks on the member.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore when it comes to swellings: if you administer any stictching medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, sarsaparilla, senna, and the likes; or whatever among these things you choose, or all together, mix them with stictching wine or with enough egg or with garlic; and apply them on the swellings in poultices, bind them well, do not remove them by hand for days; then remove them, and start again another one until all the swellings are gone. Or you can bind it to a properly made piece of plaster; for the property of plaster is that it removes all swellings from the limbs. And if the swelling has turned hard like stone, as needing removal, if it is covered, cut away the excess and make its excess visible; or remove it with any barber until it's gone, then treat until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The member which becomes weak after confinement or imprisonment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breakage of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens due to various reasons: because it was bound too tightly and wasn't bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and couldn't come into alignment with the limb; or because of excessive swelling; or because of too large movements, not in their proper time; or because they have little blood in their body, so it's weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure involves having you eat the herbs, and make the body tender, until the healing spreads within him; then he should take baths and have fun and rest. After that, apply grease to the limb, so that the grease draws towards the major swelling, and washes it with cold water repeatedly, until the swelling aligns with the limb; and restore his natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is twisted after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if you break them open, even though the shape of the limb is distorted, it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those who say one should break the limb completely anew; many have done this in our land, and these methods are criticized, leading to great harms, perhaps even death. Nonetheless, when fractures and injuries are fresh, it's fitting that they be immersed in hot water or that medicinal plants like the leaves of basil, roots, and meadowsweet are cooked, such as with dyaquilon well made, and you use a musk paste from basil, mixed with fat from gelatine or oil of sassafras, and make a plaster out of it. Or you take greased figs, grind them with charcoal ash, and similar medications that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at no time should you rub the dislocation with wet hands continuously and for a long time. And it is advised to move the limb in each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and stiff, like bone, and needs to be treated with iron, should it come to that point where the iron has to be applied up to the bone, gently incise through the thin opening; and apply cautery and careful study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to any, if it happens now to be properly returned without injury.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the joints swell up and by chance it is set into place in its wrong position; because one should not move it at that time when they are swollen: many times it brings on pus and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If this happens, if you find a patient in such condition, let the barber-tailor tend to them first, until the abscesses have subsided; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, gently move it afterwards, and treat each member according to how they come back into place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters concerning shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat osseous at their joints and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the bottom, causing saliva from the mouth to leak out, unable to hold it, nor can they close their mouth, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When dislocations are small, they can return through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is whole and completed, you must reset it quickly, without hesitation;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a manner that the doctors cut near to the patient's head where there is flesh from the wound, and pushes the bone behind the dislocated jaw at the root of the jawbone inside the mouth if it's dislocated by half; and the other hand should be placed outside with both hands level; instruct the patient to soften their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he should gently place the bone until it returns to its place when it wakes up.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it is difficult, indeed if they are the two jaws together, so immerse them in hot water and oil, as long as you gently move them back; do not apply force during the return, just like we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed well for soothing, then place moist cloths in a poultice made from rose oil and beeswax, then bind them gently with soft threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient rest on their back, and keep their shoulders between two cushions, so they do not move nor to the right nor to the left, nor try to twist at all, but prefer light food, until the pains subside, and secure the jaws.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then test the ability to eat lightly, and make sure there is no effort in opening the mouth for eating and drinking until the mandible is well healed and clean.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be returned to their place within an hour, and are not naturally converted to their usual state, it leads to fevers that settle in, as well as abdominal distention, and sometimes vomiting of undigested food.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, death befalls the one who encounters this within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the strength
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot dislocate from within the continuous structure of it and from its bottom, and is dislocated only outside once, and one feels this well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; and then presses with their hands onto their chest, and they return it to its original position. Then place them on a plaster board and cover them up, restraining them.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head of the shoulder does not dislocate in front of the blade; if it does not, and if it does dislocate once, you must reset it to its place as we have said; then place them on a plaster board and cover them up, restraining them, and command the patient to rest until they are healthy.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in this same way is brought back the shoulder blade, when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways: one way is when it dislocates towards the part of the socket below; and the second way is at the part from the heel; and sometimes dislocates upwards on occasion, which happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inwardly through the nerves; and many times dislocates below towards the socket, even in those with little flesh, because they are quick to jump outwards; in those with enough flesh, it jumps up to its height and returns to that height.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men due to impact or fracture, and inflames the shoulder in an abscess-like manner, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you must verify it, until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And recognize dislocations when it moves towards the back, and you will make a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find clear differences between them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and from behind to the pit, at the head of the shoulder, like if it was a hole; and the patient cannot bring their hand back to their nose, nor move it in any way;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And similarly, if it is dislocated upwards and not hidden, for you will clearly find it at the pit;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation must only be done to reposition it, when it is new or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister raises his hand from the malady up, then places his fingers on the joint and lifts the joint upwards with force at the place; and the minister raises his hand and extends it upwards, placing him there; if he goes too quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said within days afterwards, then the sick person should be bathed in hot water; and the minister must gently soothe and alleviate them, as with decoction of rue and fenugreek and thyme in water, and they should be administered.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then wrap the sick person on their back, and place a pad of similar thickness under the joint, neither too soft nor too hard. Then place the heel under the pad, and lift the shoulder blade upwards, and move the head of the shoulder in a virtuous way, guiding the hand towards the ailment.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another minister cuts the neck of the patient, so that it doesn't move downwards; this shoulder now returns completely, and if you see to reset it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And make the person present at home, that he/she be larger than the patient; and face it towards the right side, and hold up one shoulder against the ribs of the patient, and lift the rib cage upwards, so that the patient hangs down in a bow-like position;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister pulls the hand of the patient downwards towards the abdomen. And if the patient is too light, place something heavy on him/her instead, and now the dislocation will return.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And you can also reset it in another way: and you should place a one-inch long stick in the ground, so that the shoulder is also placed like two bullets, and neither too big nor too greasy;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then have the patient lie on their side, but with a soft cloth under them, and let the affected area remain long and flat;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not return through all these things that we have said, then perform this treatment: take one rib from two strong pigs and four large ribs, which should allow the head to move fully into place while on its back, as follows:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then bind the trunk with a cloth underneath to prevent it from rubbing against the affected area; place it on its back under the affected area; and extend your arms along the trunk up to its full length, bind the shoulder in place on the trunk, and position your hand's arm at its base; then place your arm on one thick stick of about the same width, and keep your hands down, leaving your body hanging from the other side: the joint will now return immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, however manner, that you must place a thread equal on the joint, then apply plaster covered in powder from the mill, along with incense and yolk of egg, over the entire shoulder and around it, then remove the plaster once the process is done, and re-tie the bandage on top of the plaster, and hold the hand near its neck, and let your hands stay like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary for him to eat a little, until the limbs are strengthened, because he will heal faster; and then increase his meals after five days or seven, and move them; and if it is firm and not softened, he will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is weakened by being wet or due to another reason that it has come about, you should apply four cauterizations to it, as was described before in the chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't stay in place, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint would never settle back into its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that occurs near the buttocks and breasts, or behind, is caused by pushing and stretching of hands, and it's administered elsewhere; treatment should be given as long as one remains healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there comes stiffness in the limb, and gradual movements later on, then they should use warm baths repeatedly until this stiffness disappears, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is dislocated at its peaks and returns there; it has been dislocated from all sides, both in front and behind, and the dislocation cannot be remedied because you can see it clearly and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the shoulder bone with your sound part, if you can see it clearly. For the joint is wavy, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder to any extent.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it should be that you reset it in this manner as for pus wounds, because if pus wounds came about, there would be trouble in bringing them back; and by chance they cannot be brought back entirely, even when it is at the rear; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is as follows: when it is such that one can return it to its position, you extend your hand of his two hands; and his arms are spread out, and his hands are turned towards the center according to the circumference of the elbow from inside, outside and underneath, and force the joint back into its place together or at the base of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And when there is a dislocation of the head, it returns whenever he doubles his hand over his own hand, and brings back the elbow that has been dislocated to the base of the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it doesn't return to its place, apply strong stretching; and when both of you stretch the arm, and hold each other's hand firmly, so that it doesn't move during stretching. Then turn the arm from each side, then once you have covered a long and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you grasp the joint by hand, if you apply some oil to soften the joint, then force the joint into place until it heals.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is at its place, set it on dry plaster with the yolk of an egg, force it into position and allow the arm to hang by the neck near the body, then let it rest for a few days, then remove the bandage.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, remove the bandage and leave it as is; and if you notice that the joint does not settle well, redo the plaster and the bandage, then let it be like this for a few days until it is firmly set; then remove the bandage.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels painful after the joint is reset and it moves again, bathe and rub it nicely until it is relieved; or place a piece of fat lamb's wool on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove the bandage, and have him take a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when they sweat, you should rub the joint with precision, then place it in its original position, and afterwards immerse it in water; and thus perform this process twice or three times until it's healed; and if possible, apply moistened cow fat with butter on top, and keep it in place; it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand's joint has dislocated, and the return is slighter than with other joints. Whenever it dislocates, you should bring it back to its place immediately while it remains dislocated or when a heat abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the resetting is such that you put your hand on the diseased area on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and make them look equal, so that they place their palm against the appearance of the joint, and hold it until it realigns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Always, you should check if it is properly in place; then have the patient lie the back of their hand on a table during extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and make them place their hand against the appearance of the joint. If it returns to this position now, that means it's correctly placed.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if it's treated by removing pus with plaster poultices, and lets it continue without restarting the process.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you're unable to place it back in its position after some days, if the joint stays twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And it does no harm to the patient as long as his hands are immobilized, and he cannot hold anything at all: so know that a nerve or artery has been cut; if there is no other way but to apply a cautery in this case, and perhaps there is nothing else that matters.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in position, place it on the plaster as we have said, then apply pressure and leave it for five days, then remove it and let it be like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot be moved well, and there is no break, with hot water grease, and rub it until it becomes clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Neither are the fingers of the hand dislocated on each side, nor from the back of the palm or belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Therefore keep the fingers and prevent the dislocation in the joints until they heal. Then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part that is out of joint;
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	And let it be for two days, and then make him equal on that day; and don't leave him without lying down, as we have said, and then remove the lie from this day, and make him move, and then tie him up again at night; and do this often, until he is restricted.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do this in the same way, if it is dislocated at the wrist of the hand, and do it like you did before, until he is better; and do this similarly, when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	In the reduction of the heel, in the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When it is dislocated at the back of the heel or neck, or multiple are dislocated, if there's no treatment, because time quickens the disease.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs for this are that the evacuations happen spontaneously without control, and they cannot be held in check, and many times various parts of the body soften, or both feet or either two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And it often softens into four parts; the part that softens at the back is called 'gilbositez':
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment involves rewarding you if 'gilbositez' has come from childhood: there should be no remedy or healing until then.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling, impacts, or similar situations, according to the old methods of treatment using grandiloquent words, it does not bring any great benefit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that when the illness comes before the groin, neither disease nor healing occurs;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And also that which goes straight to the two ribs, and it cannot be cured outside of what specifically comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that diseases extend over his belly for one hand length evenly, and have strain upon him, so that he does not blister;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then insert one stick in the ground to form a cross, and another at the base, then tie a band around the joints of the muscles, and another at the hips, knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and let those who attend know about the bands, one at the head and the others at the base, among the two stakes;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the stake as we have said, and let her place her palms on the ground formed by it until she regains consciousness.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if she does not regain consciousness through this treatment, take a board of three arms long, and place it under her, and if the patient's back is straight, have her head on one side of the board. Then put the center of the board on the ground.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	Place the sights of his feet on the other end of the table and press firmly until he regains consciousness at its place; and if you can see it, perform this maneuver when turning to the hand that turns in the direction of the limb.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And when you insert two sticks at the elbow of a large limb and opposite his feet, place them so that between each stick, directly above and below, is about an inch in length.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And place two pieces of wood in each stick, or where the elbow is located, and ensure that the sticks are firmly planted in the ground so they don't move; and between every pair of sticks, place another stick turned, according to how the bone twists, and place two small sticks about an inch long between the turning sticks for twisting the elbow.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then join the two threads between the elbows and the neck, and the other thread towards the hands to the other elbow, and each servant twists their elbow for the whole length of the thread, and the master puts in an equal spine as we said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are equal, place them with a desiccant plaster and plenty of eggs, then fumigate, and then apply an ointment from a tablet of one and three quarters inches long. This should cover the area of the boil and the healthy part of the spine. Then join them with a thread as we said, using gentle stimulation until it is healthy;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if anything comes during the recovery process, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines with the fumigation we have described earlier; and whenever it's administered, use one piece of parchment.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And no appearance comes in the back vertebral spine of the back, and it should be that this is dislocation; and it's the bone which opens, so one must not have any assumption about it: by chance it could bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You should know that the joints of the hip and the shoulder can only experience dislocations alone, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: within and outward, and in front and behind; it dislocates more inwardly and less forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inwardly is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more on the diseased side than on the healthy one, and cannot bend the knee joint as far in heat.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the limb which is swollen with pus beneath it, because the head of the shoulder comes to it.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign for him who approaches fire, it is that such accidents are contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs for him who encounters ahead, it is that his leg must be well according to accomplishment; however, neither double its ankle without pain, and if one wants to make him move, he cannot beforehand, and he holds back his urine, and swells his foot, and when he walks, he does so on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs for him who encounters behind, it is that he cannot spread his ankle or double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and his foot becomes relaxed, and the head of the shoulder is in its place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The restoration of this illusion of dislocation is that you must understand that when dislocation has occurred and it remains according to its position, without any treatment, and there should not be any assumption made about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those where the dislocation is recent, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry you should return the joint, stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, no other treatment will be necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it doesn't return this way, you should apply one strong remedy, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or on a stick that is tied to the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another remedy should extend his hand on top in such a way that he pushes his hands under his armpits, then he pulls it with one strong effort against the knee; and another holds the head against the stick.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And extend both up and down at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common among four similar situations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	But if it is not like that, then you should treat according to its appearance. When the dislocation affects the paxedons (a possible term error), you must lift up the patient on their healthy side and then place a bandage at the root of the arm, followed by the elbow being above the armpit. Then, secure the bandage upwards towards the armpit, and further towards the forcele (another possible term error).
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another assistant to hold the patient's arms, and embrace the thick part of the diseased arm, stretching it upwards in form: if it returns to its normal position now; this way of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you can't compress it in this way as we have said, then you should tie the two feet of the afflicted area together with a strong rope under both the heels and under both knees, and let the affected leg extend more than 2 hands compared to the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then have it hung from the top of a post, and let there be 2 spans of length above the ground; then instruct one servant to hug onto the head of the stock, while another servants hold onto the afflicted area with their arms wrapped around the stock, for they form the stock. For the joint is now quickly returning.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is in front, if it lies to the side as we said in the one with flexibility, and holds a rope tightly on the affected leg properly, and also around the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two prongs, one on the head and another at the feet, then insert one prong between the thighs of the patient in the form;
